Rulings on the Pledgor's Acknowledgment of Third-Party Ownership
First division of iqrar in rahn: pledgor's acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings when a pledgor acknowledges that the pledged item belongs to a third party, and apply the options available to the acknowledged person and the pledgee in various scenarios of solvency and debt status.

Core Idea
A pledgor's acknowledgment of another's ownership is invalid against the pledgee's right but becomes effective once that right is removed.

When a pledgor says 'this slave belongs to so-and-so' while the slave is already pledged, the acknowledgment cannot simply be accepted because it would destroy the pledgee's security. This lesson unpacks the legal consequences: the third party can pay off the debt and take the slave, or hold the pledgor liable. It also covers what happens if the third party manumits the slave, including an important intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types of iqrar in rahn
The passage divides the topic into two: iqrar of the pledgor and iqrar of the pledgee. Focus on the first type for this lesson.
The terminology: al-rāhin (pledgor), al-murtahin (pledgee), al-muqarr lahu (acknowledged person).
2
Understand why the pledgor's iqrar is not immediately valid against the pledgee
The iqrar would nullify the pledgee's right, which is like a lien. Just as a sale or lease by the pledgor is invalid against the pledgee, so is the iqrar. Thus it is not binding on the pledgee.
The analogy is to bay‘ (sale) and ijara (lease) – these are invalid if they harm the pledgee's right.
3
Analyze the options of the acknowledged person
The acknowledged person may either (a) pay the debt and take the pledged item, then recover from the pledgor; or (b) hold the pledgor liable for the value of the item. The text explains these as analogous to the buyer paying the creditor to take the sold item.
The condition: the debt must be due. If deferred, different rules apply.
4
Examine the manumission scenario and the intra-Hanafi dispute
If the acknowledged person manumits the slave before paying, the manumission is valid because both pledgor and pledgee acknowledge him as owner or authorized. Then the pledgee may claim compensation from the manumitter according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who analogize to an authorized agent.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): if the pledgee cannot hold the manumitter liable, his recourse is only against the pledgor or the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره. صح الإقرار حقه إلى البدل على ما بينا فكان إجازته اسقاطاً لحقه فنفذ الأول لزوال المانع. وهذا إذا تعلق بالعين المرتهنة حق للغير بحق باشره الراهن، وأما لو تعلق بإقراره قال في المحيط : هذا على قسمين: أحدهما في إقرار الراهن بالمرهون للغير، والثاني في إقرار المرتهن أنه لغير الراهن. القسم الأول رهن عبداً بألف ثم قال هو لفلان لم يصدق لأن إقراره يتضمن إبطال حق المرتهن وأنه يحتمل النقض والإبطال فلم يصح في حق المرتهن كالبيع والإجارة، ثم المقر له إن شاء أدى المال وقبض الرهن لأن عدم صحة الإقرار لحق المرتهن، فإذا زال حقه كما في البيع فكما أن للمشتري أن يقضي الدين ويأخذ المبيع فكذا هذا ويرجع بما قضى على الراهن لأنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه لإحياء حقه فإنه لا يصل إلى ملكه إلا بقضاء الدين وكان كالمعير للرهن يرجع به على المستعير فكذا هذا وإن شاء ضمن الراهن قيمة العبد لأن الراهن زعم أنه ملكه رهنه بماله وسلمه بغير أمره وقد عجز عن رده إليه للحال لحق المرتهن فیضمن قيمته وللمقر أن يستحلف المرتهن على علمه لأنه ادعى عليه معنى لو أقر به لزمه، فإن أنكر استحلف عليه، وإن لم يؤدي المال وأعتق العبد جاز عتقه لأن الراهن والمرتهن تصادقا على عتق العبد لأن الراهن زعم أ أنه ملك المقر له وإعتاق المالك نافذ. والمرتهن زعم أنه كان ملك الراهن لا المقر له إلا أنه لما أقر له فقد سلطه على إعتاقه بإقراره كما لو وكله بالإعتاق . ثم المسألة على أربعة أوجه : إما أن يكون المقر له والراهن موسرين أو معسرين أو أحدهما معسر والآخر موسر والدين في ذلك كله حال أو يؤجل، فإن كان موسرين والدين حال فالمرتهن فيه بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الدين من الراهن وإن شاء ضمن المعتق القيمة ويكون رهناً، وكان يجب أن لا يكون للمرتهن تضمين المعتق على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى لأن من زعم المرتهن أنه ليس بمالك وإنما جاز عتقه بتسليط الراهن لأنه لما أقر بالملك فقد سلطه على الإعتاق فصار كما لو سلطه على الإعتاق بالوكالة فإن الراهن لو وكل وكيلاً بإعتاق المشتري قبل القبض ونقد الثمن فأعتقه الوكيل لا يضمن الوكيل عندهما فيضمن أن يكون هذا على ذلك الخلاف إذ لا فرق بينهما، ثم المعتق يما يرجع ضمن على الراهن للحال لأنه لو كان العبد قائماً كان له تضمين الراهن لما أحدث في ماله من الارتهان وتسليم ماله بغير أمره فصار غاصباً في حقه وصار ما أخذه المرتهن من المعتق ملكاً للراهن لما ضمن ذلك للمعتق بخلاف المعير إذا أعتق العبد وهو معسر والدين مؤجل فضمنة المرتهن لا يرجع به على المستعير حتى يحل الدين لأنه إنما يرجع باعتبار أنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه وقد قضى دينه المؤجل فلا يرجع بالمعجل فإذا كانا معسرين والدين حال يسعى العبد للمرتهن ويرجع على الراهن دون المعتق لأن في زعم العبد أنه لا رجوع له على المعتق لأن في زعمه أن المعتق لم متلفاً حق المرتهن بالإعتاق لأن الراهن لم يصح لأن الراهن رهن بغير أمره، وكذلك إذا كان الدين مؤجلاً. وإن كان المعتق موسراً والراهن معسراً والدين حال أو مؤجل فللمرتهن العبد لأن العتق حصل بتسليط الراهن فكان الراهن أعتقه بنفسه وهو معسر، يستسعي وإن شاء ضمن المعتق لأنه بمنزلة الوكيل عنه بالإعتاق ويرجع المعتق على الراهن لأنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه والعبد يرجع على الراهن دون المعتق وإن كان المعتق معسراً والراهن موسراً والدين حال فالراهن يأخذ بقضاء دينه، فإذا قضى الدين خرج المرتهن من الوسط فهذا رجل أعتق عبداً كله له فارغاً عارياً عن حق الغير فلا شيء على العبد، وإن كان الدين مؤجلاً فالمرتهن بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن لأنه هو المسلط على العتق فكأنه وكل المقر له بإعتاقه، وإن شاء استسعى العبد والعبد يرجع على الراهن لأنه أوفى الدين لا على المعتق لما بينا. وأما القسم الثاني فهو على وجهين : إما إن أقر المرتهن برقبة الرهن لرجل أو أقر بدين في رقبته، وكل وجه لا يخلو من ثلاثة أوجه إما أن يفتكه الراهن أو يهلك الرهن أو يباع الرهن بالدين؛ فإن أقر برقبته لرجل وقال الرهن لفلان اغتصبه الراهن فإن افتكه الراهن فلا سبيل للمقر على العبد ولا على ما أخذه المرتهن لأن إقرار المرتهن لا يصح في حق الراهن لأنه إقرار على الغير وما أخذه ليس بدلاً عن الرهن بل هو دينه استوفاه، وإن كان هلك في يد المرتهن ضمن جميع قيمته للمقر له وبطل دينه لأنه لما أن الراهن اغتصبه من فلان ورهنه منه فقد زعم الغاصب أو غاصب الغاصب وأياماً كان فهو غاصب بخلاف ما لو أفتكه لأنه إلى يد من أخذ منه فيبرأ . الضمان ويبطل دينه لأن إقراره في حق الراهن لم يصح فصح عن الرهن في حقه. وأما إذا العبد أما الراهن أو العدل وأخذ المرتهن الثمن فإن أجاز المقر له بيع أخذه من المرتهن، وإن لم يجز فلا لأن من زعم المرتهن أن العبد للمقر له وقد البيع إذنه فيكون موقوفاً على إجازته، فإن أجاز يكون ثمن ،عبد، وإن لم يجز فليس بثمن عبده ولا سبيل له عليه، وإن أقر بدين عليه لرجل؛ إن أفتكه الراهن وأخذ منه العبد فلا ضمان على المرتهن لأنه رد العبد إلى من أخذ منه فإن هلك في يده يرجع المقر له على المرتهن بدينه لا غير. ولم يفصل في الكتاب بين ما إذا وجب دين المقر له قبل الرهن أو بعده، وقيل هذا إذا وجب دينه قبل الرهن وإن وحب بعده فلا شيء للمقر له على المرتهن لأن بالهلاك استوفى دينه من مالية العبد، فإذا كان الدين واجباً قبل رهنه تبين أنه استوفى دينه ومالية العبد دين على العبد وجب استيفاؤه ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى، فأما إذا وجب الدين بعد رهنه فحينئذ صار مستوفياً دينه من ماليته ليس في مالية العبد دين وجب استيفاؤه فصح الاستيفاء. وأما إذا العبد في الدين فللمقر له أن يأخذ الثمن من المرتهن أجاز البيع أو لم يجز، لأن بيع البيع ههنا جائز لأنه ملك للمقر له في العبد، وإذا جاز البيع يقوم الثمن مقامه. ومن زعم المرتهن أن المقر له أحق بثمن العبد منه لأن دينه دين العبد ودين المولى ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى فيدفعه إليه .
As for the Book of Pledge, Chapter on Disposition in the Pledge, Injury upon it, and its Injury upon others. The acknowledgment is valid, [but] his right is [limited] to the substitute as we explained, so his permission [of the acknowledgment] is a cancellation of his right, thus the first [act] became effective due to the removal of the impediment. This is when a right of another is attached to the pledged property due to a right that the pledgor directly undertook. But if it is related to his acknowledgment, he said in al-Muhit: This is of two types: one is the acknowledgment of the pledgor that the pledged item belongs to another; the second is the acknowledgment of the pledgee that it is not the pledgor's. First type: He pledged a slave for one thousand then said, 'He belongs to so-and-so,' he is not believed because his acknowledgment entails nullifying the right of the pledgee, and it is subject to revocation and nullification, so it is not valid concerning the right of the pledgee, like sale and lease. Then the acknowledged person, if he wishes, may pay the debt and take possession of the pledge because the invalidity of the acknowledgment is due to the right of the pledgee; so when his right ceases, as in sale, just as the buyer may pay the debt and take the sold item, so too here, and he recovers from the pledgor what he paid because he paid his debt and is forced to do so to revive his right, for he cannot obtain ownership except by paying the debt. This is like the lender of the pledge who recovers from the borrower; so too here. And if he wishes, he may hold the pledgor liable for the value of the slave because the pledgor claimed that it was his own, pledged it for his debt, and delivered it without his permission, and he is unable to return it to him at present due to the pledgee's right, so he is liable for its value. And the acknowledged person may ask the pledgee to take an oath regarding his knowledge because he claims against him a matter that, if he acknowledged it, would be binding on him. If he denies, he is made to take an oath. If he does not pay the debt and manumits the slave, his manumission is valid because the pledgor and the pledgee agree on the manumission of the slave: the pledgor claims that he is the property of the acknowledged person, and the owner's manumission is effective; the pledgee claims that he was the property of the pledgor, not the acknowledged person, but since he acknowledged him, he has authorized him to manumit him by his acknowledgment, as if he had appointed him as agent for manumission. Then the issue has four aspects: either the acknowledged person and the pledgor are both solvent, or both insolvent, or one insolvent and the other solvent, and the debt in all that is either due or deferred. If both are solvent and the debt is due, the pledgee has the choice: if he wishes, he takes the debt from the pledgor; if he wishes, he holds the manumitter liable for the value, and it remains a pledge. According to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), the pledgee should not have the option to hold the manumitter liable because the pledgee claims that he is not the owner, and the manumission is valid only by the authorization of the pledgor, since when he acknowledged ownership, he authorized him to manumit, so it is as if he authorized him to manumit by agency. For if the pledgor appointed an agent to manumit the buyer before taking delivery and paying the price, and the agent manumitted him, the agent is not liable according to them. Thus this follows that difference, for there is no distinction between them. Then the manumitter, when he [the pledgee] holds him liable, recovers from the pledgor immediately because if the slave were still extant, he would have the right to hold the pledgor liable for what he caused to his property by pledging and delivering his property without his permission, so he becomes a usurper with respect to him, and what the pledgee took from the manumitter becomes the property of the pledgor because he guaranteed that for the manumitter, unlike the case of the lender if he manumits the slave while insolvent and the debt is deferred, and the pledgee holds him liable, he does not recover from the borrower until the debt becomes due, because he recovers on the basis that he paid his debt under compulsion, and he has paid a deferred debt, so he does not recover an accelerated amount. If both are insolvent and the debt is due, the slave works [to earn] for the pledgee and recovers from the pledgor, not from the manumitter, because in the slave's view, he has no recourse against the manumitter, because in his view the manumitter did not destroy the pledgee's right by manumission, because the pledgor did not [authorize?] because the pledgor pledged without his permission. Similarly if the debt is deferred. If the manumitter is solvent and the pledgor insolvent, and the debt is due or deferred, the pledgee [may take] the slave because the manumission occurred by the pledgor's authorization, so the pledgor himself manumitted him, and he is insolvent, so the slave works [to pay]; and if he wishes, he may hold the manumitter liable because he is like his agent for manumission, and the manumitter recovers from the pledgor because he paid his debt under compulsion, and the slave recovers from the pledgor, not from the manumitter. If the manumitter is insolvent and the pledgor solvent, and the debt is due, the pledgor takes [the slave] to pay his debt; when he pays the debt, the pledgee exits the picture. This is a man who manumitted a slave entirely his own, free and clear of anyone else's right, so nothing is owed by the slave. If the debt is deferred, the pledgee has the choice: if he wishes, he holds the pledgor liable because he is the one who authorized the manumission, as if he appointed the acknowledged person as agent to manumit; if he wishes, he makes the slave work, and the slave recovers from the pledgor because he paid the debt, not from the manumitter as explained. As for the second type, it has two aspects: either the pledgee acknowledges the corpus of the pledge to a person, or he acknowledges a debt against it. Each aspect has three possibilities: either the pledgor ransoms it, or the pledge perishes, or the pledge is sold for the debt. If he acknowledges the corpus to a person and says, 'The pledge belongs to so-and-so; the pledgor seized it from him,' then if the pledgor ransoms it, the acknowledged person has no claim against the slave nor against what the pledgee took, because the acknowledgment of the pledgee is not valid concerning the right of the pledgor, for it is an acknowledgment against another, and what he took is not a substitute for the pledge but rather his debt which he collected. If it perished in the hands of the pledgee, he is liable for the full value to the acknowledged person, and his debt is void because when the pledgor seized it from so-and-so and pledged it from him, he is deemed a usurper or a usurper's usurper, whichever, he is a usurper. Unlike if he ransoms it, because [he returns it] to the hand from which he took it, so he is free from liability, and his debt is void because his acknowledgment concerning the pledgor was not valid, so it is valid concerning the slave with respect to him. As for if the slave [is sold] by the pledgor or the trustee, and the pledgee takes the price, then if the acknowledged person permits the sale, he takes it from the pledgee; if he does not permit, he does not, because the pledgee claims that the slave belongs to the acknowledged person, and he did not authorize the sale, so it is suspended pending his permission. If he permits, it is the price of his slave; if he does not permit, it is not the price of his slave, and he has no claim to it. If he acknowledges a debt against him to a person: if the pledgor ransoms and takes the slave, there is no liability on the pledgee because he returned the slave to the one from whom he took it. If it perishes in his hand, the acknowledged person recovers from the pledgee his debt, nothing more. The book did not distinguish between whether the debt of the acknowledged person was obligatory before the pledge or after. It is said: this is if his debt was obligatory before the pledge; if it was obligatory after, the acknowledged person has no recourse against the pledgee because by the destruction he collected his debt from the slave's value. So if the debt was obligatory before his pledge, it becomes clear that he collected his debt, and the slave's value is a debt against the slave that must be collected, and the slave's debt takes precedence over the owner's debt. As for if the debt was obligatory after his pledge, then he has collected his debt from his value; there is no debt in the slave's value that must be collected, so the collection is valid. As for if the slave [is sold] for debt, the acknowledged person may take the price from the pledgee whether he permits the sale or not, because the sale here is valid since the slave is owned by the acknowledged person, and if the sale is valid, the price takes its place. And the pledgee claims that the acknowledged person is more entitled to the price of the slave than him, because his debt is a debt of the slave, and the owner's debt, and the slave's debt takes precedence over the owner's debt, so he pays it to him.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the rulings on acknowledgment (iqrar) in the context of a pledged property (rahn). It presents two main divisions: first, the acknowledgment of the pledgor (rahin) that the pledged item belongs to a third party; second, the acknowledgment of the pledgee (murtahin) that the item does not belong to the pledgor. Under each, the author details scenarios depending on the solvency of parties and the nature of the debt (due or deferred).

The first division: If a pledgor acknowledges that the pledged slave belongs to another, this acknowledgment is not valid against the pledgee because it would affect his right. However, the acknowledged person (muqarr lahu) has options: he may pay off the debt and take the slave, recovering the amount from the pledgor; or he may hold the pledgor liable for the slave's value. If the slave is manumitted (either by the acknowledged person as owner or by the pledgor with permission), the manumission is valid, and the pledgee may claim compensation from the manumitter or the slave depending on solvency. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the pledgee can claim compensation from the manumitter, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say he cannot, analogizing to the case of an agent authorized to manumit.

The second division: If the pledgee acknowledges that the slave belongs to another, his acknowledgment is invalid against the pledgor because it is an acknowledgment against another (iqrar 'ala al-ghayr). If the pledgor ransoms the slave, the acknowledged person has no claim. If the slave perishes, the pledgee is liable for its full value to the acknowledged person, and his debt against the pledgor is void. If the slave is sold, the sale is suspended pending the acknowledged person's permission. If the pledgee acknowledges a debt against the slave (e.g., the slave owes money), the ruling depends on whether the debt existed before or after the pledge.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission of a right or ownership; in this context, it is a statement by the pledgor or pledgee regarding the ownership of the pledged item.
الراهن (al-rāhin): The pledgor, the person who gives an item as security for a debt.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The pledgee, the person who receives the item as security for a debt.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made; the alleged owner or creditor.
المعتق (al-mu’tiq): The manumitter, the person who frees the slave; in this context, the acknowledged person who manumits the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the first division (pledgor's acknowledgment), if the acknowledged person manumits the slave before paying the debt, what is the status of the manumission?
A) The manumission is invalid because the acknowledged person is not the owner.
B) The manumission is valid only if the pledgee agrees.
C) The manumission is valid because both the pledgor and the pledgee have consented (the pledgor by the acknowledgment, the pledgee by his silence).
D) The manumission is valid but the slave remains subject to the pledge.

Key Takeaway
A pledgor's acknowledgment of a third party's ownership is conditionally valid; it is ineffective against the pledgee's right until that right is removed or compensated, and the third party has multiple options to enforce his ownership.

intermediate
10 min
Rulings on the Pledgee's Acknowledgment of Third-Party Ownership
Second division of iqrar in rahn: pledgee's acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the pledgee's acknowledgment of the corpus and acknowledgment of a debt against the pledged item, and apply the rulings for three outcomes: ransom, perishing, and sale.

Core Idea
The pledgee's acknowledgment is invalid against the pledgor because it is an iqrar against another, but it binds the pledgee himself as if he were a usurper.

If the pledgee says, 'this slave belongs to Zaid, not the pledgor,' his statement does not harm the pledgor's rights. Instead, the acknowledgment may create liability for the pledgee if the slave perishes. This lesson unpacks the two subcategories: acknowledgment of ownership and acknowledgment of a debt, each with scenarios of ransom, destruction, and sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two subcategories of the pledgee's iqrar
The pledgee may acknowledge that the pledged item's corpus belongs to a third party, or that a debt is owed against the item (e.g., the slave owes money). Each has different rules.
For the first subcategory, the pledgee says 'the slave is for Zaid, the pledgor seized it from him.' For the second, he says 'the slave owes money to Zaid.'
2
Analyze the first subcategory: acknowledgment of corpus ownership
The pledgee's acknowledgment is not valid against the pledgor (it is iqrar 'ala al-ghayr). So if the pledgor ransoms the item, the third party has no claim. If the item perishes, the pledgee is liable for its full value to the third party, and his debt is void. If sold, the sale is suspended pending the third party's permission.
The key principle: the pledgee's acknowledgment binds him like a confession of being a usurper if the item is destroyed.
3
Analyze the second subcategory: acknowledgment of a debt against the item
If the pledgee says the slave owes money to Zaid, and the slave perishes, the third party can claim only his debt from the pledgee, nothing more. The distinction depends on whether the debt existed before or after the pledge.
If the debt preceded the pledge, the pledgee is deemed to have collected his own debt from the slave's value, so the third party's debt takes priority. If after, the pledgee's collection is valid.
4
Apply the ruling to the sale scenario
If the slave is sold by the pledgor or trustee, and the pledgee takes the price, the third party acknowledged as owner may take the price if he permits the sale; otherwise, the sale is void as to him. If he is acknowledged as a creditor, he may take the price directly because his debt has priority.
The difference between ownership and debt becomes clearest in the sale outcome.

Source Text

أما كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره. صح الإقرار حقه إلى البدل على ما بينا فكان إجازته اسقاطاً لحقه فنفذ الأول لزوال المانع. وهذا إذا تعلق بالعين المرتهنة حق للغير بحق باشره الراهن، وأما لو تعلق بإقراره قال في المحيط : هذا على قسمين: أحدهما في إقرار الراهن بالمرهون للغير، والثاني في إقرار المرتهن أنه لغير الراهن. القسم الأول رهن عبداً بألف ثم قال هو لفلان لم يصدق لأن إقراره يتضمن إبطال حق المرتهن وأنه يحتمل النقض والإبطال فلم يصح في حق المرتهن كالبيع والإجارة، ثم المقر له إن شاء أدى المال وقبض الرهن لأن عدم صحة الإقرار لحق المرتهن، فإذا زال حقه كما في البيع فكما أن للمشتري أن يقضي الدين ويأخذ المبيع فكذا هذا ويرجع بما قضى على الراهن لأنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه لإحياء حقه فإنه لا يصل إلى ملكه إلا بقضاء الدين وكان كالمعير للرهن يرجع به على المستعير فكذا هذا وإن شاء ضمن الراهن قيمة العبد لأن الراهن زعم أنه ملكه رهنه بماله وسلمه بغير أمره وقد عجز عن رده إليه للحال لحق المرتهن فیضمن قيمته وللمقر أن يستحلف المرتهن على علمه لأنه ادعى عليه معنى لو أقر به لزمه، فإن أنكر استحلف عليه، وإن لم يؤدي المال وأعتق العبد جاز عتقه لأن الراهن والمرتهن تصادقا على عتق العبد لأن الراهن زعم أ أنه ملك المقر له وإعتاق المالك نافذ. والمرتهن زعم أنه كان ملك الراهن لا المقر له إلا أنه لما أقر له فقد سلطه على إعتاقه بإقراره كما لو وكله بالإعتاق . ثم المسألة على أربعة أوجه : إما أن يكون المقر له والراهن موسرين أو معسرين أو أحدهما معسر والآخر موسر والدين في ذلك كله حال أو يؤجل، فإن كان موسرين والدين حال فالمرتهن فيه بالخيار إن شاء أخذ الدين من الراهن وإن شاء ضمن المعتق القيمة ويكون رهناً، وكان يجب أن لا يكون للمرتهن تضمين المعتق على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى لأن من زعم المرتهن أنه ليس بمالك وإنما جاز عتقه بتسليط الراهن لأنه لما أقر بالملك فقد سلطه على الإعتاق فصار كما لو سلطه على الإعتاق بالوكالة فإن الراهن لو وكل وكيلاً بإعتاق المشتري قبل القبض ونقد الثمن فأعتقه الوكيل لا يضمن الوكيل عندهما فيضمن أن يكون هذا على ذلك الخلاف إذ لا فرق بينهما، ثم المعتق يما يرجع ضمن على الراهن للحال لأنه لو كان العبد قائماً كان له تضمين الراهن لما أحدث في ماله من الارتهان وتسليم ماله بغير أمره فصار غاصباً في حقه وصار ما أخذه المرتهن من المعتق ملكاً للراهن لما ضمن ذلك للمعتق بخلاف المعير إذا أعتق العبد وهو معسر والدين مؤجل فضمنة المرتهن لا يرجع به على المستعير حتى يحل الدين لأنه إنما يرجع باعتبار أنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه وقد قضى دينه المؤجل فلا يرجع بالمعجل فإذا كانا معسرين والدين حال يسعى العبد للمرتهن ويرجع على الراهن دون المعتق لأن في زعم العبد أنه لا رجوع له على المعتق لأن في زعمه أن المعتق لم متلفاً حق المرتهن بالإعتاق لأن الراهن لم يصح لأن الراهن رهن بغير أمره، وكذلك إذا كان الدين مؤجلاً. وإن كان المعتق موسراً والراهن معسراً والدين حال أو مؤجل فللمرتهن العبد لأن العتق حصل بتسليط الراهن فكان الراهن أعتقه بنفسه وهو معسر، يستسعي وإن شاء ضمن المعتق لأنه بمنزلة الوكيل عنه بالإعتاق ويرجع المعتق على الراهن لأنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه والعبد يرجع على الراهن دون المعتق وإن كان المعتق معسراً والراهن موسراً والدين حال فالراهن يأخذ بقضاء دينه، فإذا قضى الدين خرج المرتهن من الوسط فهذا رجل أعتق عبداً كله له فارغاً عارياً عن حق الغير فلا شيء على العبد، وإن كان الدين مؤجلاً فالمرتهن بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن لأنه هو المسلط على العتق فكأنه وكل المقر له بإعتاقه، وإن شاء استسعى العبد والعبد يرجع على الراهن لأنه أوفى الدين لا على المعتق لما بينا. وأما القسم الثاني فهو على وجهين : إما إن أقر المرتهن برقبة الرهن لرجل أو أقر بدين في رقبته، وكل وجه لا يخلو من ثلاثة أوجه إما أن يفتكه الراهن أو يهلك الرهن أو يباع الرهن بالدين؛ فإن أقر برقبته لرجل وقال الرهن لفلان اغتصبه الراهن فإن افتكه الراهن فلا سبيل للمقر على العبد ولا على ما أخذه المرتهن لأن إقرار المرتهن لا يصح في حق الراهن لأنه إقرار على الغير وما أخذه ليس بدلاً عن الرهن بل هو دينه استوفاه، وإن كان هلك في يد المرتهن ضمن جميع قيمته للمقر له وبطل دينه لأنه لما أن الراهن اغتصبه من فلان ورهنه منه فقد زعم الغاصب أو غاصب الغاصب وأياماً كان فهو غاصب بخلاف ما لو أفتكه لأنه إلى يد من أخذ منه فيبرأ . الضمان ويبطل دينه لأن إقراره في حق الراهن لم يصح فصح عن الرهن في حقه. وأما إذا العبد أما الراهن أو العدل وأخذ المرتهن الثمن فإن أجاز المقر له بيع أخذه من المرتهن، وإن لم يجز فلا لأن من زعم المرتهن أن العبد للمقر له وقد البيع إذنه فيكون موقوفاً على إجازته، فإن أجاز يكون ثمن ،عبد، وإن لم يجز فليس بثمن عبده ولا سبيل له عليه، وإن أقر بدين عليه لرجل؛ إن أفتكه الراهن وأخذ منه العبد فلا ضمان على المرتهن لأنه رد العبد إلى من أخذ منه فإن هلك في يده يرجع المقر له على المرتهن بدينه لا غير. ولم يفصل في الكتاب بين ما إذا وجب دين المقر له قبل الرهن أو بعده، وقيل هذا إذا وجب دينه قبل الرهن وإن وحب بعده فلا شيء للمقر له على المرتهن لأن بالهلاك استوفى دينه من مالية العبد، فإذا كان الدين واجباً قبل رهنه تبين أنه استوفى دينه ومالية العبد دين على العبد وجب استيفاؤه ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى، فأما إذا وجب الدين بعد رهنه فحينئذ صار مستوفياً دينه من ماليته ليس في مالية العبد دين وجب استيفاؤه فصح الاستيفاء. وأما إذا العبد في الدين فللمقر له أن يأخذ الثمن من المرتهن أجاز البيع أو لم يجز، لأن بيع البيع ههنا جائز لأنه ملك للمقر له في العبد، وإذا جاز البيع يقوم الثمن مقامه. ومن زعم المرتهن أن المقر له أحق بثمن العبد منه لأن دينه دين العبد ودين المولى ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى فيدفعه إليه .
As for the Book of Pledge, Chapter on Disposition in the Pledge, Injury upon it, and its Injury upon others. The acknowledgment is valid, [but] his right is [limited] to the substitute as we explained, so his permission [of the acknowledgment] is a cancellation of his right, thus the first [act] became effective due to the removal of the impediment. This is when a right of another is attached to the pledged property due to a right that the pledgor directly undertook. But if it is related to his acknowledgment, he said in al-Muhit: This is of two types: one is the acknowledgment of the pledgor that the pledged item belongs to another; the second is the acknowledgment of the pledgee that it is not the pledgor's. First type: He pledged a slave for one thousand then said, 'He belongs to so-and-so,' he is not believed because his acknowledgment entails nullifying the right of the pledgee, and it is subject to revocation and nullification, so it is not valid concerning the right of the pledgee, like sale and lease. Then the acknowledged person, if he wishes, may pay the debt and take possession of the pledge because the invalidity of the acknowledgment is due to the right of the pledgee; so when his right ceases, as in sale, just as the buyer may pay the debt and take the sold item, so too here, and he recovers from the pledgor what he paid because he paid his debt and is forced to do so to revive his right, for he cannot obtain ownership except by paying the debt. This is like the lender of the pledge who recovers from the borrower; so too here. And if he wishes, he may hold the pledgor liable for the value of the slave because the pledgor claimed that it was his own, pledged it for his debt, and delivered it without his permission, and he is unable to return it to him at present due to the pledgee's right, so he is liable for its value. And the acknowledged person may ask the pledgee to take an oath regarding his knowledge because he claims against him a matter that, if he acknowledged it, would be binding on him. If he denies, he is made to take an oath. If he does not pay the debt and manumits the slave, his manumission is valid because the pledgor and the pledgee agree on the manumission of the slave: the pledgor claims that he is the property of the acknowledged person, and the owner's manumission is effective; the pledgee claims that he was the property of the pledgor, not the acknowledged person, but since he acknowledged him, he has authorized him to manumit him by his acknowledgment, as if he had appointed him as agent for manumission. Then the issue has four aspects: either the acknowledged person and the pledgor are both solvent, or both insolvent, or one insolvent and the other solvent, and the debt in all that is either due or deferred. If both are solvent and the debt is due, the pledgee has the choice: if he wishes, he takes the debt from the pledgor; if he wishes, he holds the manumitter liable for the value, and it remains a pledge. According to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), the pledgee should not have the option to hold the manumitter liable because the pledgee claims that he is not the owner, and the manumission is valid only by the authorization of the pledgor, since when he acknowledged ownership, he authorized him to manumit, so it is as if he authorized him to manumit by agency. For if the pledgor appointed an agent to manumit the buyer before taking delivery and paying the price, and the agent manumitted him, the agent is not liable according to them. Thus this follows that difference, for there is no distinction between them. Then the manumitter, when he [the pledgee] holds him liable, recovers from the pledgor immediately because if the slave were still extant, he would have the right to hold the pledgor liable for what he caused to his property by pledging and delivering his property without his permission, so he becomes a usurper with respect to him, and what the pledgee took from the manumitter becomes the property of the pledgor because he guaranteed that for the manumitter, unlike the case of the lender if he manumits the slave while insolvent and the debt is deferred, and the pledgee holds him liable, he does not recover from the borrower until the debt becomes due, because he recovers on the basis that he paid his debt under compulsion, and he has paid a deferred debt, so he does not recover an accelerated amount. If both are insolvent and the debt is due, the slave works [to earn] for the pledgee and recovers from the pledgor, not from the manumitter, because in the slave's view, he has no recourse against the manumitter, because in his view the manumitter did not destroy the pledgee's right by manumission, because the pledgor did not [authorize?] because the pledgor pledged without his permission. Similarly if the debt is deferred. If the manumitter is solvent and the pledgor insolvent, and the debt is due or deferred, the pledgee [may take] the slave because the manumission occurred by the pledgor's authorization, so the pledgor himself manumitted him, and he is insolvent, so the slave works [to pay]; and if he wishes, he may hold the manumitter liable because he is like his agent for manumission, and the manumitter recovers from the pledgor because he paid his debt under compulsion, and the slave recovers from the pledgor, not from the manumitter. If the manumitter is insolvent and the pledgor solvent, and the debt is due, the pledgor takes [the slave] to pay his debt; when he pays the debt, the pledgee exits the picture. This is a man who manumitted a slave entirely his own, free and clear of anyone else's right, so nothing is owed by the slave. If the debt is deferred, the pledgee has the choice: if he wishes, he holds the pledgor liable because he is the one who authorized the manumission, as if he appointed the acknowledged person as agent to manumit; if he wishes, he makes the slave work, and the slave recovers from the pledgor because he paid the debt, not from the manumitter as explained. As for the second type, it has two aspects: either the pledgee acknowledges the corpus of the pledge to a person, or he acknowledges a debt against it. Each aspect has three possibilities: either the pledgor ransoms it, or the pledge perishes, or the pledge is sold for the debt. If he acknowledges the corpus to a person and says, 'The pledge belongs to so-and-so; the pledgor seized it from him,' then if the pledgor ransoms it, the acknowledged person has no claim against the slave nor against what the pledgee took, because the acknowledgment of the pledgee is not valid concerning the right of the pledgor, for it is an acknowledgment against another, and what he took is not a substitute for the pledge but rather his debt which he collected. If it perished in the hands of the pledgee, he is liable for the full value to the acknowledged person, and his debt is void because when the pledgor seized it from so-and-so and pledged it from him, he is deemed a usurper or a usurper's usurper, whichever, he is a usurper. Unlike if he ransoms it, because [he returns it] to the hand from which he took it, so he is free from liability, and his debt is void because his acknowledgment concerning the pledgor was not valid, so it is valid concerning the slave with respect to him. As for if the slave [is sold] by the pledgor or the trustee, and the pledgee takes the price, then if the acknowledged person permits the sale, he takes it from the pledgee; if he does not permit, he does not, because the pledgee claims that the slave belongs to the acknowledged person, and he did not authorize the sale, so it is suspended pending his permission. If he permits, it is the price of his slave; if he does not permit, it is not the price of his slave, and he has no claim to it. If he acknowledges a debt against him to a person: if the pledgor ransoms and takes the slave, there is no liability on the pledgee because he returned the slave to the one from whom he took it. If it perishes in his hand, the acknowledged person recovers from the pledgee his debt, nothing more. The book did not distinguish between whether the debt of the acknowledged person was obligatory before the pledge or after. It is said: this is if his debt was obligatory before the pledge; if it was obligatory after, the acknowledged person has no recourse against the pledgee because by the destruction he collected his debt from the slave's value. So if the debt was obligatory before his pledge, it becomes clear that he collected his debt, and the slave's value is a debt against the slave that must be collected, and the slave's debt takes precedence over the owner's debt. As for if the debt was obligatory after his pledge, then he has collected his debt from his value; there is no debt in the slave's value that must be collected, so the collection is valid. As for if the slave [is sold] for debt, the acknowledged person may take the price from the pledgee whether he permits the sale or not, because the sale here is valid since the slave is owned by the acknowledged person, and if the sale is valid, the price takes its place. And the pledgee claims that the acknowledged person is more entitled to the price of the slave than him, because his debt is a debt of the slave, and the owner's debt, and the slave's debt takes precedence over the owner's debt, so he pays it to him.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the rulings on acknowledgment (iqrar) in the context of a pledged property (rahn). It presents two main divisions: first, the acknowledgment of the pledgor (rahin) that the pledged item belongs to a third party; second, the acknowledgment of the pledgee (murtahin) that the item does not belong to the pledgor. Under each, the author details scenarios depending on the solvency of parties and the nature of the debt (due or deferred).

The first division: If a pledgor acknowledges that the pledged slave belongs to another, this acknowledgment is not valid against the pledgee because it would affect his right. However, the acknowledged person (muqarr lahu) has options: he may pay off the debt and take the slave, recovering the amount from the pledgor; or he may hold the pledgor liable for the slave's value. If the slave is manumitted (either by the acknowledged person as owner or by the pledgor with permission), the manumission is valid, and the pledgee may claim compensation from the manumitter or the slave depending on solvency. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the pledgee can claim compensation from the manumitter, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani say he cannot, analogizing to the case of an agent authorized to manumit.

The second division: If the pledgee acknowledges that the slave belongs to another, his acknowledgment is invalid against the pledgor because it is an acknowledgment against another (iqrar 'ala al-ghayr). If the pledgor ransoms the slave, the acknowledged person has no claim. If the slave perishes, the pledgee is liable for its full value to the acknowledged person, and his debt against the pledgor is void. If the slave is sold, the sale is suspended pending the acknowledged person's permission. If the pledgee acknowledges a debt against the slave (e.g., the slave owes money), the ruling depends on whether the debt existed before or after the pledge.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission; here, the pledgee's statement that the pledged item belongs to another or owes a debt.
الراهن (al-rāhin): The pledgor.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The pledgee.
المقر له (al-muqarr lahu): The third party in whose favor the acknowledgment is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under the second division, if the pledgee acknowledges that the corpus of the pledge belongs to a third party and the pledgor then ransoms the item, what is the third party's right?
A) The third party can take the item from the pledgor.
B) The third party can claim compensation from the pledgee.
C) The third party has no claim because the pledgee's acknowledgment is invalid against the pledgor.
D) The third party must wait until the debt is paid.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee's acknowledgment is binding on himself but not on the pledgor; the third party's recourse is against the pledgee only, and depends on whether the item perishes, is ransomed, or sold.

Rulings on Creditor's Acknowledgment of a Third Party's Right in the Pawn
Rulings for creditor's acknowledgment of third party rights on pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for each scenario when a creditor acknowledges a third party's ownership or debt on a pawn.

Core Idea
A creditor's acknowledgment of another's right binds him, but its effect varies with redemption, destruction, or sale.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh details the consequences when a creditor (مرتهن) declares that the pawned item belongs to someone else or has a debt owed to someone else. The rulings are conditional on three events: the debtor redeems the pawn, the pawn is destroyed, or it is sold. We will dissect these conditions and their implications, focusing on the principles of acknowledgment against another (إقرار على الغير) and priority of the slave's debt.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of acknowledgment
Identify whether the creditor acknowledges ownership (رقبة الرهن) or a debt (دين في رقبته) of the pawn. Each type has distinct rulings.
2
For each type, identify three events
The three events are: redemption by the debtor, destruction of the pawn in the creditor's hand, and sale of the pawn for the debt. These trigger different legal consequences.
3
Apply rulings for ownership acknowledgment
For each event: if redeemed, the third party has no claim; if destroyed, the creditor pays full value and loses his debt; if sold, the third party may take the proceeds if he ratifies the sale.
4
Apply rulings for debt acknowledgment
For debt, distinguish timing: if the debt was due before the pawn, the creditor is liable; if after, no liability. For sale, the third party always takes the price.
5
Note the underlying principles
The creditor's acknowledgment is not valid against the debtor (إقرار على الغير), and the slave's debt takes priority over the master's debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني فهو على وجهين: إما إن أقر المرتهن برقبة الرهن لرجل أو أقر بدين في رقبته، وكل وجه لا يخلو من ثلاثة أوجه: إما أن يفتكه الراهن أو يهلك الرهن أو يباع الرهن بالدين. فإن أقر برقبته لرجل وقال الرهن لفلان اغتصبه الراهن فإن افتكه الراهن فلا سبيل للمقر على العبد ولا على ما أخذه المرتهن لأن إقرار المرتهن لا يصح في حق الراهن لأنه إقرار على الغير وما أخذه ليس بدلاً عن الرهن بل هو دينه استوفاه، وإن كان هلك في يد المرتهن ضمن جميع قيمته للمقر له وبطل دينه لأنه لما أن الراهن اغتصبه من فلان ورهنه منه فقد زعم الغاصب أو غاصب الغاصب وأيما كان فهو غاصب بخلاف ما لو أفتكه لأنه إلى يد من أخذ منه فيبرأ الضمان ويبطل دينه لأن إقراره في حق الراهن لم يصح فصح عن الرهن في حقه. وأما إذا بيع العبد إما الراهن أو العدل وأخذ المرتهن الثمن فإن أجاز المقر له البيع أخذه من المرتهن، وإن لم يجز فلا لأن من زعم المرتهن أن العبد للمقر له وقد البيع بإذنه فيكون موقوفاً على إجازته، فإن أجاز يكون ثمن عبده، وإن لم يجز فليس بثمن عبده ولا سبيل له عليه. وإن أقر بدين عليه لرجل: إن افتكه الراهن وأخذ منه العبد فلا ضمان على المرتهن لأنه رد العبد إلى من أخذ منه، فإن هلك في يده يرجع المقر له على المرتهن بدينه لا غير. ولم يفصل في الكتاب بين ما إذا وجب دين المقر له قبل الرهن أو بعده، وقيل هذا إذا وجب دينه قبل الرهن وإن وجب بعده فلا شيء للمقر له على المرتهن لأن بالهلاك استوفى دينه من مالية العبد، فإذا كان الدين واجباً قبل رهنه تبين أنه استوفى دينه ومالية العبد دين على العبد وجب استيفاؤه ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى، فأما إذا وجب الدين بعد رهنه فحينئذ صار مستوفياً دينه من ماليته ليس في مالية العبد دين وجب استيفاؤه فصح الاستيفاء. وأما إذا بيع العبد في الدين فللمقر له أن يأخذ الثمن من المرتهن أجاز البيع أو لم يجز، لأن بيع البيع ههنا جائز لأنه ملك للمقر له في العبد، وإذا جاز البيع يقوم الثمن مقامه. ومن زعم المرتهن أن المقر له أحق بثمن العبد منه لأن دينه دين العبد ودين المولى ودين العبد مقدم على دين المولى فيدفعه إليه. بغير بيع
As for the second division, it is of two types: either the creditor acknowledges the ownership of the pawn to a man, or he acknowledges a debt on it. Each type has three scenarios: either the debtor redeems it, or the pawn perishes, or the pawn is sold for the debt. If he acknowledges its ownership to a man and says: 'The pawn belongs to so-and-so; the debtor usurped it,' then if the debtor redeems it, the acknowledged party has no claim against the slave nor against what the creditor took, because the creditor's acknowledgment is not valid against the debtor as it is an acknowledgment against another, and what he took is not a substitute for the pawn but his debt collected. If it perishes in the creditor's hand, he guarantees its entire value to the acknowledged party and his debt is void, because since the debtor usurped it from so-and-so and pawned it to him, he is considered a usurper or a second usurper; whichever, he is a usurper, unlike if he had redeemed it because he returned it to the one from whom he took it, so he is released from liability and his debt is void, because his acknowledgment against the debtor was not valid, so it becomes valid as against the pawn in his favor. As for if the slave is sold – either by the debtor or the trustee – and the creditor takes the price, then if the acknowledged party ratifies the sale, he takes from the creditor; if he does not, then no, because the creditor claims that the slave belongs to the acknowledged party but the sale was with his permission, so it is suspended on his ratification; if he ratifies, it is the price of his slave; if he does not, it is not the price of his slave and he has no claim to it. And if he acknowledges a debt on him to a man: if the debtor redeems and takes the slave, there is no liability on the creditor because he returned the slave to the one from whom he took; if it perishes in his hand, the acknowledged party has recourse against the creditor for his debt only. And the book did not distinguish between whether the acknowledged party's debt was due before the pawn or after; it is said this is if his debt was due before the pawn, but if it was due after, then the acknowledged party has nothing against the creditor, because by the destruction he collected his debt from the slave's value; so if the debt was due before the pawn, it becomes clear that he collected his debt, and the slave's value is a debt on the slave, and the slave's debt is prior to the master's debt. However, if the debt was due after the pawn, then he has collected his debt from his value, and there is no debt in the slave's value to collect, so the collection is valid. And if the slave is sold for the debt, then the acknowledged party may take the price from the creditor whether or not he ratified the sale, because the sale here is valid as the slave is owned by the acknowledged party, and if the sale is valid, the price takes its place. And the creditor claims that the acknowledged party is more entitled to the slave's price than him, because his debt is a debt on the slave, and the slave's debt takes precedence over the master's debt, so he pays it to him. Without sale.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the consequences when the creditor (مرتهن) acknowledges that the pawned slave is owned by a third party or owes a debt to a third party. It is divided into two types: acknowledgment of ownership and acknowledgment of a debt. For each type, three scenarios are considered: the debtor redeems the pawn, the pawn perishes, or the pawn is sold for the debt. The rulings are intricate and depend on the validity of the creditor's acknowledgment against the debtor and the timing of the third party's right. For example, if the creditor acknowledges ownership and the pawn perishes in his hand, he must pay the full value to the third party and loses his own debt. If the debtor redeems, the third party has no claim. For acknowledgment of debt, the creditor's liability depends on whether the debt was due before or after the pawn. The text also discusses the sale: if the slave is sold, the third party (acknowledged owner) can take the price from the creditor. The passage is packed with conditional rulings typical of Hanafi fiqh, requiring careful parsing. All examples are strictly within the Hanafi madhhab, and the reasoning is based on principles like the invalidity of acknowledgment against another (إقرار على الغير) and priority of the slave's debt over the master's debt.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment; a declaration by the creditor that another has a right in the pawn.
مقر له (muqarr lah): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made (the third party).
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; taking property illegally. Used here to describe the debtor's acquisition of the slave.
دين العبد (dayn al-'abd): Debt owed by the slave (e.g., from trade or injury). It takes priority over the master's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor acknowledges that the pawn is owned by a third party and the pawn perishes in the creditor's hand, what is the ruling?
A) The creditor guarantees the full value to the third party and his debt is void.
B) The creditor loses only his debt, no guarantee.
C) The third party has no claim because the debtor is the owner.
D) The creditor must return the pawn's value to the debtor.

Key Takeaway
A creditor's acknowledgment of a third party's right in a pawn binds him personally, but the effect on his claim and liability depends on the specific event (redemption, destruction, or sale) and the timing of the third party's right.

Effectiveness of Manumitting a Pawned Slave: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on debtor's manumission of pawned slave with proof and scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a debtor's manumission of a pawned slave and explain the scenarios based on the debtor's wealth and debt timing.

Core Idea
Manumission of a pawned slave is effective, but the creditor's security shifts to the slave's value or his earnings.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical question: can a debtor free a slave that he has pledged as collateral? The answer is yes, but with conditions. The ruling protects both the slave's freedom and the creditor's right, illustrating how Hanafi fiqh balances competing interests through substitution mechanisms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the different scenarios
List all combinations of debtor/manumitter wealth (wealthy/insolvent) and debt status (due/deferred). Note how the ruling changes for each.
Focus on the variables: wealth of the one who actually manumits (mu'tiq) and the debtor (rahin).
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, determine what happens to the creditor, the slave, and the manumitter. Use the text to map the outcomes.
Pay attention to the options for the creditor (e.g., hold liable, take value, make slave work).
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the qiyas used: analogy to manumission of a sold slave before delivery, a runaway, a usurped slave. Identify the asl, far', and illa.
The text explicitly cites 'as if he manumitted a sold slave before delivery or a runaway or a usurped slave.'
4
Understand the illa
The effective cause is that the debtor's ownership of the slave is stronger than the creditor's possessory right. Since manumission is based on ownership, it prevails.
The text argues: 'ownership of the physical slave is stronger than the possessory right.'
5
See the practical consequences
Apply the ruling: if the debtor is wealthy, the slave's value is taken as a pledge; if insolvent, the slave works to pay the lesser of his value or the debt.
This substitution preserves the creditor's security while freeing the slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان المعتق موسراً والراهن معسراً والدين حال أو مؤجل فللمرتهن العبد لأن العتق حصل بتسليط الراهن فكان الراهن أعتقه بنفسه وهو معسر، يستسعي وإن شاء ضمن المعتق لأنه بمنزلة الوكيل عنه بالإعتاق ويرجع المعتق على الراهن لأنه قضى دينه وهو مضطر فيه والعبد يرجع على الراهن دون المعتق وإن كان المعتق معسراً والراهن موسراً والدين حال فالراهن يأخذ بقضاء دينه، فإذا قضى الدين خرج المرتهن من الوسط فهذا رجل أعتق عبداً كله له فارغاً عارياً عن حق الغير فلا شيء على العبد، وإن كان الدين مؤجلاً فالمرتهن بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الراهن لأنه هو المسلط على العتق فكأنه وكل المقر له بإعتاقه، وإن شاء استسعى العبد والعبد يرجع على الراهن لأنه أوفى الدين لا على المعتق لما بينا. ولو مؤجلاً أخذ قيمة العبد وجعلت رهناً مكانه ولو معسراً سعى العبد في الإقل من قيمته ومن الدين. قال رحمه الله: (ونفذ عتقه) أي نفذ عتق الراهن وهو قول الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى وفي قول آخر لا ينفذ موسراً كان أو معسراً لأن فى تنفيذه إبطال حق المرتهن. ولنا أن العتق صدر من أهله مضافاً إلى محله ملكه ووجب بنفاذه ولا يلغو تصرفه لعدم إذن المرتهن كما إذا أعتق المبيع قبل القبض أو الآبق أو المغصوب، وإذا زال ملك الراهن عن رقبته بإعتاقه يزول ملك المرتهن لأنه بناء عليه كإعتاق العبد المشترك بل أولى لأن ملك الرقبة أقوى من اليد، فإذا لم يمتنع الأعلى فالأدنى أولى أن لا يمنعه. ولا يلزمنا إعتاق الوارث العبد الموصي برقبته إذا لم يكن له مال آخر حيث إنه لا ينفذ مع أنه أعتق ملكه لأنا نقول: يعتق عند الثاني والثالث في الحال. وعند الإمام يؤخر إلى أداء السعاية على ما عرف في إعتاق العبد المشترك ولم يكن إعتاقه لغواً وهو ههنا جعله لغواً. ولا يقال المرهون كالخارج عن ملك الراهن بدليل أن المولى إذا أتلفه يجب عليه ضمانه فكذا لا ينفذ عتقه لأنه خرج عن ملكه لأنا نقول: الضمان عليه باعتبار أنه إذا أتلف المالية المشغولة بحق المرتهن كالمولى يتلف عبده المأذون له فإنه يضمن قيمته للغرماء مع بقاء ملكه فيه من كل وجه، ولهذا ينفذ تصرفه فيه. ولو قال المؤلف ونفذ تدبيره لكان أولى إذا علم نفاذ التدبير من الراهن والتدبير أدنى حالاً من الاستيلاد علم نفاذ الاستيلاء والإعتاق من باب أولى. قال في المبسوط: إعتاق الراهن وتدبيره واستيلاده ينفذ ويضمن القيمة ويكون رهناً مكانه إن كان موسراً، ثم إن كان المال حالاً اقتضاه من القيمة، وإن كان الراهن معسراً فللراهن استسعاء المدبر وأم الولد في جميع الدين والمعتق في قيمته ثم يرجع المعتق بما أدى على المولى. قال رحمه الله: (وطولب بدينه لو حالا) يعني إذا كان الدين حالاً طالب المرتهن الراهن بعد العتق بالدين إذا كان موسراً لأنه إذا طولب بالرهن كان له أن يأخذه بدينه إذا كان من جنس حقه فيكون إيفاء واستيفاء فلا فائدة فيه. قال رحمه الله: (ولو مؤجلاً أخذ قيمة العبد وجعلت رهناً مكانه) يعني لو كان الدين مؤجلاً يؤخذ من المعتق قيمة العبد وتجعل رهناً مكان العبد إذا كان موسراً لأن قد تحقق، وفي التضمين فائدة وهي حصول الاستيثاق من الوجه الذي بيناه ويحبسها إلى حلول الأجل، فإذا حل اقتضاه بحقه إذا كان بجنسه لأن للغريم أن يستوفي حقه من غريمه إذا ظفر بجنس حقه، وإن كان فيه فضل رده لانتهاء حكم الرهن بالاستيفاء، وإن كان حقه أقل من القيمة رجع بالزيادة لعدم ما يسقطه. قال رحمه الله: (ولو معسراً سعى العبد في الأقل من قيمته ومن الدين) لأن حق المرتهن كان متعلقاً به فإذا تعذر الرجوع على المعتق لعسره عليه لأنه رجع هو المنتفع بهذا العتق كما في عتق أحد الشريكين العبد المشترك، لأن الضمان بالجراح والغرم بالغنم. وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أنه يسعى في الأقل من الشيئين المذكورين والمنقول في غيره أنه يسعى في الأقل من ثلاثة أشياء. قال في الجامع: أصله أن الراهن إذا سبب الضمان من مال
And if the manumitter is wealthy and the debtor is insolvent and the debt is due or deferred, then the creditor takes the slave because the manumission occurred by the debtor's authorization; thus the debtor manumitted him himself while insolvent, so the slave works for the debt, and if he wishes, he can hold the manumitter liable because he is like an agent for the debtor in manumission, and the manumitter recovers from the debtor because he paid his debt under compulsion, and the slave recovers from the debtor not the manumitter. And if the manumitter is insolvent and the debtor is wealthy and the debt is due, then the debtor takes to pay his debt; when he pays, the creditor drops out; this is a man who manumitted a slave entirely his own, free of any third party right, so nothing is owed by the slave. And if the debt is deferred, the creditor has the option: if he wishes, he holds the debtor liable because he authorized the manumission, as if he appointed the recipient as agent for manumitting, and if he wishes he makes the slave work for the debt, and the slave recovers from the debtor because he paid the debt, not from the manumitter as we explained. And if deferred, the value of the slave is taken and made a pledge in his place; and if insolvent, the slave works to pay the lesser of his value and the debt. He (the author) said: (And his manumission is effective), meaning the debtor's manumission is effective, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). In another opinion it is not effective whether the debtor is wealthy or insolvent because executing it voids the creditor's right. Our proof: The manumission issued from one qualified, attached to its proper place which is his property, and it is obligatory to give effect, and his action is not nullified for lack of the creditor's permission, just as if he manumitted a sold slave before delivery, or a runaway, or a usurped slave. And if the debtor's ownership of the slave is removed by his manumission, the creditor's right is also removed because it is built upon it, like the manumission of a jointly owned slave, indeed more so because ownership of the physical slave is stronger than the possessory right, so if the stronger does not prevent, the weaker is more entitled not to prevent. And we are not compelled by the case of the heir manumitting a slave whose usufruct was bequeathed when he has no other property, where it is not effective even though he manumitted his property, because we say: it becomes effective at the second and third step immediately, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is delayed until the slave earns, as known in the manumission of a jointly owned slave, and his manumission was not void – here he makes it void. And it cannot be said that the pawn is like outside the debtor's ownership, as evidence that if the master destroys it, he must guarantee it, so likewise his manumission should not be effective because it left his ownership. We say: the guarantee is upon him because when he destroys the financial value encumbered by the creditor's right, like a master destroying his slave who is permitted to trade, he guarantees its value to the creditors while his ownership remains fully; therefore his disposal is effective. And if the author had said 'and his tadbir is effective' it would be more appropriate, since tadbir (contract of deferred manumission) from the debtor is effective, and tadbir is lower in status than istilad (giving birth to a child), so istilad and manumission are effective a fortiori. He said in al-Mabsut: The debtor's manumission, tadbir, and istilad are effective, and he guarantees the value, and it becomes a pledge in its place if he is wealthy; then if the debt is due, he takes the value; if the debtor is insolvent, the debtor has the right to make the mudabbar and umm walad work to pay the entire debt, and the manumitted slave works for his value, then the manumitted slave recovers what he paid from the master. He (the author) said: (And he is demanded for his debt if it is due) meaning that if the debt is due, the creditor demands the debtor after manumission if he is wealthy, because if he demands the pawn, he can take it for his debt if it is of the same genus, so it would be payment and collection, so no benefit. He (the author) said: (And if deferred, the value of the slave is taken and made a pledge in its place) meaning if the debt is deferred, the value of the slave is taken from the manumitter and made a pledge in place of the slave if he is wealthy because the guarantee is realized, and in holding liable there is benefit of obtaining security in the manner we explained, and he keeps it until the term ends; when it ends, he takes it for his right if of the same genus, because a creditor can take his right from his debtor if he finds the same genus, and if there is surplus, he returns it because the pledge is terminated by collection, and if his right is less than the value, he gets the balance because there is nothing to void it. He (the author) said: (And if insolvent, the slave works to pay the lesser of his value and the debt) because the creditor's right was attached to him, so if it is not possible to recover from the manumitter due to his insolvency, the slave works because he is the one benefiting from this manumission, just as in the manumission of a jointly owned slave by one partner, because liability is according to injury and profit. And the apparent wording of the author is that he works to pay the lesser of the two mentioned things, but it is transmitted elsewhere that he works to pay the lesser of three things. He said in al-Jami': The origin is that if the debtor is the cause of the guarantee from wealth.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the effectiveness of a debtor's manumission of a pawned slave. It opens by detailing various scenarios based on the financial status of the debtor and the manumitter (the one who actually performs the manumission, often the creditor or a third party) and the nature of the debt (due or deferred). The core ruling is that the manumission is effective, and the creditor's right is transferred to the slave's value or the slave's earning. The author then provides the proof (dalil) for this ruling, citing the Hanafi position and refuting the opposing view. The key analogy is to a manumitted slave before delivery or a runaway slave, and to a jointly owned slave. The author explains that the debtor's ownership is superior to the creditor's possessory right, so manumission is not prevented. The discussion concludes with practical applications: if the debtor is wealthy, the value of the slave is taken and made a pledge; if insolvent, the slave works to pay the lesser of his value or the debt. The passage is dense and uses technical terms like 'isstis'aa' (earning) and 'tadbir' (deferred manumission). All examples and rulings strictly follow the Hanafi madhhab, with references to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's works.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): Manumission; freeing a slave by the owner's declaration.
استسعاء (istis'aa'): Earning; requiring the slave to work to pay off a debt or value.
موسر (muyassir): Wealthy; having sufficient assets to pay the debt or value.
معسر (mu'sir): Insolvent; lacking assets to pay; then the slave must earn.
قيمة العبد (qimat al-'abd): The market value of the slave, used as substitute for the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the proof (dalil) for the effectiveness of the debtor's manumission of a pawned slave?
A) A direct Quranic verse.
B) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions.
C) Analogy (qiyas) to manumission of a sold slave before delivery, a runaway, or a usurped slave.
D) Custom ('urf) of the people.

Key Takeaway
The debtor's manumission of a pawned slave is effective, with the creditor's right shifting to the slave's value or his earnings, based on the priority of ownership over possessory right.

Lender's Specification of Pledge and Violation Thereof
Sharh on ruling when lender specifies pledge terms and borrower or pledgee violates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on violation of a lender's beneficial specification of pledge terms, and identify the lender's options and the legal basis for liability.

Core Idea
Violating a beneficial pledge specification makes the violator liable as a usurper.

In this passage, the commentator explains the ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq on what happens when a lender (mu'ir) specifies how the borrowed item should be pledged, and the borrower or pledgee violates that specification. The key is that the specification must be beneficial (mufid) to the lender; violation amounts to transgression (ta'addi), giving the lender a choice to hold either party liable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its trigger
Determine the exact scenario: lender (mu'ir) specifies amount, type, or location for the pledge. The borrower or pledgee violates that specification. The ruling gives the lender two options.
2
Understand the analogy to usurper (ghasib)
The commentator likens the violator to a usurper: the borrower is like a ghasib, and the pledgee like a usurper of the usurper. The legal basis is transgression (ta'addi) against the owner's right.
Qiyas jaliy: the illa is ta'addi.
3
Recognize the exception when specification is not beneficial
If the lender specified an amount greater than the item's value, and the borrower pledged it for less (but still at least the value), the borrower is not liable because the specification was not beneficial; it was harmful due to difficulty of payment.
The ruling applies only when the specification is beneficial (mufid).
4
Determine the lender's choice and its consequences
Lender may hold either the borrower or pledgee liable for the value. If borrower is held liable, he becomes owner and his pledge becomes of his own property. If pledgee is held liable, he can recover from the original pledgor.
Lender cannot hold both simultaneously; must choose one.
5
Apply the ruling to a simple case
Work through a scenario: lender specifies City A, borrower pledges in City B. The lender may choose to hold the borrower for the value, or the pledgee. Explain why each is a transgressor.
This step consolidates the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ولو عين قدراً أو جنساً أو بلداً فخالف ضمن المعير المستعير أو المرتهن) أي لو عين المعير قدر ما يرهنه به أو جنسه أو البلد الذي يرهنه فيه فخالف كان المعير بالخيار إن شاء ضمن المستعير قيمته. وإن شاء ضمن المرتهن لأن كل واحد منهما متعد في حقه فصار الراهن كالغاصب والمرتهن كغاصب الغاصب، وإنما كان كذلك لأن التقييد مفيد وهو نفي الزيادة لأن غرضه الاحتباس بما تيسر أداؤه وبقي النقصان أيضاً لأن غرضه أن مستوفياً للأكثر بمقابلته عند الهلاك ليرجع عليه بالكثير والنقصان يمنع من ذلك فيكون متعدياً فيضمن إلا إذا عين له أكثر من قيمته فرهنه بأقل من ذلك بمثل قيمته أو أكثر لا أدائه يضمن لأنه خلاف إلى خير لأن غرضه من الرجوع عليه بأكثر حاصل بذلك مع لأنه لم يرجع إلا بقدر القيمة لأن الاستيفاء لم يقع إلا به فتعييبه أكثر من قيمته غير مفيد في حقه بل فيه ضرر عليه لتعسر أدائه، وكذلك التقييد بالجنس والشخص والبلد لأن كل ذلك مفيد لتيسير بعض الأجناس في التحصيل دون البعض وتفاوت الأشخاص والبلدان في الحفظ والإعانة فيضمن بالمخالفة، فلو قال ضمن حيث كان التقييد مفيداً لكان أولى لأن الإطلاق غير مستقيم فإذا ضمن المستعير ثم عقد الرهن بينه وبين المرتهن لأنه ملكه بأداء الضمان فتبين أنه رهن ملك نفسه، وإن ضمن المرتهن رجع المرتهن بما ضمن وبالدين على الراهن على ما بيناه في الاستحقاق وقد تقدم له مزید بیان فراجعه
He said, may God have mercy on him: (And if he specified a quantity or a type or a city, and he violated, then the lender may hold liable the borrower or the pledgee). Meaning: if the lender specified the amount with which he would pledge it, or its type, or the city in which he would pledge it, and he violated, then the lender has the choice: if he wishes he holds the borrower liable for its value, and if he wishes he holds the pledgee liable, because each of them is a transgressor with respect to his right. So the pledgor becomes like a usurper and the pledgee like a usurper of the usurper. And it is thus only because the restriction is beneficial: it denies excess because his purpose is retention with what can be easily paid; and also the deficiency remains because his purpose is that he would have recourse for more when it perishes by its value so he can claim a lot, and deficiency prevents that, so he is transgressing and thus liable. Unless he specified more than its value, and he pledged it for less than that, even if it is equal to its value or more, he is not liable because that is a violation towards good, because his purpose of recourse for more is achieved by that (since he only takes the value anyway because fulfillment only occurs to the extent of the value). So specifying more than its value is not beneficial in his right; rather there is harm upon him due to difficulty of payment. Similarly for specification by type, person, and city, because all that is beneficial for ease of collection of some types over others, and differences of persons and cities in preservation and assistance, so he is liable for violation. So if he said 'liable' where the restriction is beneficial, it would be more appropriate, because the absolute is not correct. If he holds the borrower liable, then the borrower makes a contract of pledge between himself and the pledgee because he owns it by paying the liability, so it becomes clear that it is a pledge of his own property. If he holds the pledgee liable, the pledgee recovers what he paid in liability and the debt from the pledgor, as we explained in the case of istihqaq; and its detailed explanation has preceded, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling states: if the lender (mu'ir) specifies a particular amount, type, or city for the pledge (rahn), and the borrower (musta'ir) or the pledgee (murtahin) violates that specification, the lender may hold either one liable for the value of the borrowed item. The reasoning is that the specification is beneficial (mufid) for the lender's purpose: he wants the pledge to be easily redeemable and to have recourse for the maximum possible value in case of loss. Violating it is an act of transgression (ta'addi). The commentary explains an exception: if the lender specified an amount greater than the item's value, and the borrower pledged it for a lesser amount — even as low as its value or more — the borrower is not liable, because the lender's goal of having recourse for a higher value is still achieved (since he can only recover up to the value). Moreover, specifying more than the value is not beneficial but rather harmful due to difficulty of payment. The commentary also clarifies that if the borrower is held liable, he becomes the owner of the item by paying the liability, so his subsequent pledge is of his own property. If the pledgee is held liable, he can recover what he paid plus the debt from the original pledgor (the borrower).

Key Terms
المعير (al-mu'ir): The lender who gives an item as a loan (aariyah) for the purpose of being pledged.
المستعير (al-musta'ir): The borrower who receives the item as a loan (aariyah) and then pledges it as collateral.
التقييد (al-taqyid): A restriction placed by the lender on how the item is to be pledged, whether by amount, type, or location.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lender specifies that the borrowed item should be pledged for 100 dirhams, but the borrower pledges it for 80 dirhams, what is the lender's right?
A) The lender can only hold the borrower liable.
B) The lender can hold either the borrower or the pledgee liable for the value.
C) The lender cannot hold anyone liable because the pledge is valid.
D) The lender can demand the item back from the pledgee without compensation.

Key Takeaway
When a lender's beneficial pledge specification is violated, he may choose to hold either the borrower or the pledgee liable for the value.

Pledge Perishes at Pledgee When Specification Followed
Sharh on ruling when borrower complies with specification and pledge perishes at pledgee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pledged item perishes at the pledgee after the borrower follows the lender's specification, and identify the correct compensation for qimi items.

Core Idea
When a pledged item perishes at the pledgee after compliance, the debt is discharged and the borrower owes the lender the item's value.

This commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a specific scenario in pledge law. Understanding this ruling clarifies how possession (qabd) affects liability and how compensation is calculated for non-fungible items. The commentator refines the matn's wording to ensure precise legal terminology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Recognise that the borrower (musta'ir) follows the lender's (mu'ir) specification, and the pledged item perishes in the pledgee's (murtahin) hands. The ruling: the pledgee becomes a fulfiller (mustawfi), the pledgor's debt is discharged, and the borrower owes compensation to the lender.
This is the core hukm from the matn.
2
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Understand why this ruling applies: the pledgee's possession is qabd istifa' (possession for fulfillment), so destruction completes the fulfillment, analogous to a creditor receiving payment and then losing it.
Qabd istifa' is distinct from trust or liability possession.
3
Examine the correction of terminology
The commentator corrects the matn's use of 'mithl' (equivalent) to 'qimah' (value) for qimi items like cloth. Distinguish between mithli (fungible) and qimi (non-fungible) property.
This correction ensures accurate legal expression.
4
Apply the ruling to a defective pledge
The passage also states that if the pledge's value decreases due to a defect, the debt is reduced proportionally. Apply the same principle: the lender recovers from the pledgor the reduced amount.
This shows consistency in the legal framework.

قال رحمه الله : (وإن وافق وهلك عند المرتهن صار مستوفياً ووجب مثله للمعير على المستعير لأن قبض الرهن قبض استيفاء وبالهلاك يتم الاستيفاء فيسقط الدين عن الراهن ويضمن للمعير قيمته لأن قضى بذلك القدر دينه إن كان كله مضموناً وإلا يضمن قدر المضمون والباقي أمانة وهذا ظاهر، وكذا لو نقصت قيمة الرهن بعيب أصابه يذهب من الدين بحسابه ويرجع المعير بذلك على الراهن لما ذكرنا . وقول المؤلف ووجب مثله ليس بظاهر لأن الثوب من القيمي لا من المثلي، وقول ملا مسكين أي وجب مثل الدين للمعير على المستعير كلام فاسد لأن الواجب للمعير على المستعير هنا قيمة الثوب ولو قال وجب بدله لكان أولى والله أعلم.
He said, may God have mercy on him: (And if he complied and it perished in the possession of the pledgee, he becomes a fulfiller and its equivalent becomes due to the lender from the borrower) because the taking of the pledge is a taking for fulfillment, and with destruction the fulfillment is completed, so the debt falls from the pledgor, and he (the borrower) guarantees to the lender its value because he (the lender) paid that amount of his debt. If the whole debt was secured, then he guarantees the whole; otherwise he guarantees the amount secured, and the rest is a trust. This is apparent. Likewise, if the value of the pledge decreases due to a defect occurring, the debt is reduced proportionally, and the lender recovers that from the pledgor as mentioned. The author's saying 'its equivalent' is not apparent because the cloth is a qimi (value-based) item, not a mithli (fungible). The saying of Mulla Miskin that 'the equivalent of the debt is due to the lender from the borrower' is corrupt speech, because what is due to the lender from the borrower here is the value of the cloth. If he said 'its substitute' it would be better. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling for the case where the borrower follows the lender's specification and the pledged item perishes in the pledgee's hands. The ruling is that the pledgee's possession becomes a 'possession of fulfillment' (qabd istifa'), meaning he is deemed to have received his debt in full. Thus, upon the item's destruction, the debtor's debt (which he owes to the lender, i.e., the person who lent the item? Actually careful: The scenario is: A borrows an item from B (mu'ir) to pledge it to C (murtahin) as collateral for a loan A takes from C. So when B sets terms, A follows them and pledges the item to C. The item perishes at C. Then C is considered to have 'fulfilled' his debt to A? Wait, the text says the opposite: "فيسقط الدين عن الراهن" meaning the debt of the pledgor (A) falls. And then the borrower (A) must pay the lender (B) the value (or equivalent) of the borrowed item. Actually careful: The matn says "صار مستوفياً ووجب مثله للمعير على المستعير" meaning the pledgee (C) becomes 'mustawfiyan' (one who has received his due), and an equivalent becomes due to the lender (B) from the borrower (A). This is because B's item was used to fulfill A's debt to C, so A owes B the item's value. The commentary clarifies that 'mithl' (equivalent) refers to the specific item if it is a fungible, but here the example is a cloth, which is a qimi (value) item, so it should be 'value' (qimah). The commentator corrects the matn's wording, stating that 'badal' (substitute) would be more accurate.

Key Terms
قبض استيفاء (qabd istifa'): A form of possession that is deemed to fulfill a right, such that destruction during this possession is equivalent to having received the right itself.
قيمي (qimi): A property that has significant variance in value among individuals, such that compensation is determined by market value rather than by a standard equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentator correct in the matn?
A) The term 'mustawfi' should be 'mustawdi'
B) The compensation is 'mithl' not 'qimah'
C) The compensation is 'qimah' not 'mithl'
D) The debt is not discharged

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a pledged item perishes at the pledgee after compliance, the debt is discharged and the borrower owes the lender the item's value, with precise compensation depending on whether the item is mithli or qimi.
