Pawned Slave Kills Another Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pawned slave killing another slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on the effect of handing over a killer pawned slave, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Handing over a killer pawned slave does not reduce the debt according to Abu Hanifa; the substitute is identical in substance.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pawned slave that kills another slave. The central question: does handing over the killer slave to the creditor reduce the debt, or must the full debt still be paid? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold one view; Muhammad and Zufar offer alternatives. Understanding their reasoning is key to applying Hanafi pawn law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What exactly is disputed? The effect of handing over a killer slave on the debt obligation of the rahin (pawner).
The killer slave is given to the creditor in place of the original pawn.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that the killer slave does not reduce the debt; the rahin must pay the full debt to redeem the pawn.
Their reasoning: the second slave takes the place of the first in flesh and blood; market price fluctuations do not affect the debt.
3
State the positions of Muhammad and Zufar
Muhammad gives the rahin an option: either pay full debt or hand over the killer slave as full satisfaction. Zufar holds that the killer becomes an additional pawn for its value, reducing the debt proportionally.
Muhammad analogizes to sale and usurpation; Zufar sees the killer as a new pawn.
4
Analyze the proofs
Compare the qiyas to sale and usurpation (Muhammad's proof) and the response that the killer is a substitute in substance, not a change in the pawn itself.
The Hanafi response: change in price is not change in essence; the substitute is legally identical.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the killer slave is handed over, does the debt remain or get reduced according to each imam?
Mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: debt remains full.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن قتله عبد قيمته مائة فدفعه به افتكه بكل الدين) وهذا قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد : هو بالخيار إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين، وإن شاء دفع العبد المدفوع إلى المرتهن بدينه ولاشيء عليه غيره. وقال زفر يصير رهناً بمائة وسقط من الدين بقدر الغاية. قلنا إن العبد الثاني قام مقام الأول لحماً ودماً ولو كان الأول قائماً وانتقص السعر لا ينقص الدين وهي على الخلاف ولمحمد أن المرهون تغير في ضمان المرتهن فيخير الراهن كالبيع والمغصوب إذا كان قيمة كل واحد منهما ألف وقتل كل واحد منهما عبداً قيمته مائة أن كل واحد من المشتري والمغصوب منه بالخيار إن شاء أخذ القاتل ولا شيء له غيره، وإن شاء فسخ المشتري البيع ورجع المغصوب منه بقيمة العبد، ولهما أن التغيير لم يظهر في نفس العبد لقيام الثاني مقام الأول لحماً ودماً لا يجوز تمليكه من المرتهن بغير رضاه، وعلى هذا الخلاف لو تراجع سعره حتى صار يساوي مائة ثم قتل عبداً يساوي مائة فدفع به.
He (the author) said: (If a slave kills another slave, the killer being worth one hundred, and he hands him over, he redeems the pawn with the entire debt.) This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He has the option: if he wishes, he redeems with the full debt, or he hands over the killer slave to the creditor in satisfaction of the debt and nothing else is owed. Zufar said: The killer becomes a pawn for one hundred and a corresponding amount of the debt is reduced. We (the Hanafis) say: The second slave takes the place of the first in flesh and blood, and if the first had remained and its price decreased, the debt would not reduce. The dispute is based on this. According to Muhammad, the pawned object has changed while in the creditor's possession, so the pawner has an option, like in sale and usurpation: if each of two slaves is worth one thousand and each kills a slave worth one hundred, then both the buyer and the person from whom the property was usurped have a choice: either take the killer and nothing else, or the buyer may rescind the sale and the usurped person may claim the value of the slave. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the change does not appear in the slave itself because the second slave takes the place of the first in flesh and blood; it is not permissible to transfer ownership to the creditor without his consent. And on this difference, if the market price rises and then falls back to one hundred and then the slave kills another slave worth one hundred and is handed over, the same difference applies.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pawned slave who kills another slave. The key issue is whether handing over the killer slave to the creditor is sufficient to redeem the pawn or whether the full debt must be paid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the rahin must pay the entire debt because the killer slave is merely a substitute for the original pawn and does not constitute a reduction of the debt. Muhammad gives the rahin a choice: either pay the full debt or hand over the killer slave as full satisfaction. Zufar holds that the killer slave becomes an additional pawn and reduces the debt proportionally. The text provides a rational analogy to sale and usurpation (ghasp) to support Muhammad's view, but Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter that the change is not in the essence of the slave but in its market condition, which does not affect the debt obligation. The mufta bihi view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
ضمان المرتهن (daman al-murtahin): The liability of the creditor (mortgagee) for the pawned item while in his possession.
قيام مقام (qiyam maqam): Taking the place of; substitution of the killer slave for the original pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a pawned slave kills another slave and the killer is handed over to the creditor, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt is fully discharged.
B) The debt is reduced by the killer's value.
C) The debt remains and the rahin must pay the full amount to redeem.
D) The debt is voided entirely.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi pawn law, a slave that kills another does not reduce the debt when handed over; the substitute is considered identical in substance.

Pawning Grape Juice That Becomes Wine Then Vinegar
Ruling on pawn validity with transformation of substance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a pawned item that transforms into a different substance and explain why quantity, not value, determines debt reduction for measured items.

Core Idea
For measured items, debt reduction depends on quantity, not value, even if the substance transforms.

This lesson examines a nuanced case: pawning grape juice that turns into wine then vinegar. The central ruling is that the pawn remains valid for the original debt as long as the quantity remains unchanged. The passage clarifies that for measured commodities (makil/mawzun), changes in value are irrelevant; only loss of quantity reduces the debt. We will walk through the reasoning and the critical refinement of the basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
State the scenario: a Muslim pawns grape juice worth ten for a debt of ten. It becomes wine, then vinegar, still worth ten. The ruling: it remains a pawn for ten.
The ruling is initially based on the salability of the final substance.
2
Understand the initial reasoning
The initial reasoning: 'What is legally salable as an existing commodity is valid as a pawn.' Wine is salable as an existing commodity for dhimmis, so by extension, the pawn remains valid.
This reasoning covers the transformation from juice to wine, but the commentator asks: why mention the final step to vinegar?
3
Locate the critical refinement
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) challenges the reliance on value in the phrase 'it is worth ten'. He argues that for measured items (grape juice and vinegar), the criterion is quantity, not value.
The refinement is supported by the analogy of a broken heart-shaped pawn where weight (quantity) remains.
4
Apply the qiyas
The analogy: if a heart-shaped pawn breaks but its weight remains, the debt is unchanged. Similarly, if juice becomes vinegar but quantity remains, the debt is unchanged.
The illa (effective cause) is that the substance (ain) remains despite change in description.
5
Distinguish the dhimmi case
If both pawner and creditor are dhimmis, the pawn of wine that becomes vinegar remains valid even if value decreases, because the substance remains. The pawner then has the option to redeem with full debt or claim similar wine.
This shows that for dhimmis, the ruling is even more lenient regarding value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل هذا الفصل بمنزلة المتفرقة المذكورة في أواخر الكتب فلذا أخره استدراكاً لما فاته فيما سبق . قال رحمه الله : رهن عصيراً قيمته عشرة بعشرة فتخمر ثم تخلل وهو يساوي عشرة فهو رهن بعشرة) يعني إذا رهن عند مسلم عصيراً إلى آخرها قالوا ما كان محلاً للبيع بقاء يكون محلاً للرهن بقاء كما أن ما يكون محلاً للبيع ابتداء يكون محلاً للرهن ابتداء والخمر محل للبيع بقاء وإن لم يكن محلاً له ابتداء ، أقول : لقائل أن يقول لو كان مدار مسألتنا المذكورة على هذا القدر من التعليل لما ظهر فائدة قوله ثم صار خلاً في وضع مسألة بل كان يكفي أن يقال ومن رهن عصيراً بعشرة فتخمر فهو رهن بعشرة لكفاية التعليل المذكور بعينه في إثبات هذا المعنى العام فتأمل . قال صاحب العناية : ولقائل أن يقول ما يرجع إلى المحل فالابتداء والبقاء فيه سواء فما بال هذا ذلك الأصل؟ وقال : ويمكن أن يجاب عنه بأنه كذلك فيما يكون المحل باقياً وههنا يتبدل المحل حكماً بتبدل الوصف فكذلك تخلف عن ذلك الأصل ا هـ . . أقول : قوله : «ثم تخلل وهي تساوي عشرة» يشير إلى أن المعتبر فيه في الزيادة والنقصان القيمة وليس كذلك بل المعتبر القدر لأن العصير والخل من المقدرات لأنه إما مكيل أو موزون وفيها نقصان القيمة لا يوجب سقوط شيء من ذلك الدين كما مر في انكسار القلب، وإنما يوجب الخيار على ما ذكرنا لأن الغاية فيه مجرد الوصف وفوات كل شيء من الوصف في المكيل والموزون لا يوجب سقوط شيء من الدين بإجماع بين أصحابنا فيكون الحكم فيه أنه إن نقص شيء من القدر سقط بقدره شيء من الدين وإلا فلا. وأشار بقوله ثم تخلل إلى أن المرهون عنده مسلم والراهن فلو كان ذمياً قال في المبسوط : رهن ذمي من ذمي خمراً فصارت خلاً لا ينقص من قيمته بقدره ويبقى رهناً لأن بالتغيير من وصف المرارة إلى الحموضة نقصت المالية عندهم ومقومها مع بقاء العين بحالها وبتبدل الصفة لا يبطل الرهن كما لو كان الرهن قلباً فانكسر وبقي الوزن على حاله، ثم عندهما يتخير الراهن إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين ،وأخذه، وإن شاء ضمنه خمراً مثل خمره فيصير
Chapter: This chapter is like the scattered issues mentioned at the end of books, so he delayed it to cover what was missed earlier. He (the author) said: If one pawns grape juice worth ten for ten, and it becomes wine, then it becomes vinegar and is worth ten, it remains a pawn for ten. Meaning: If a Muslim pawns grape juice... They said: What is legally salable as an existing commodity is legally valid as a pawn as an existing commodity, just as what is legally salable at the outset is valid as a pawn at the outset. Wine is salable as an existing commodity even though it is not salable at the outset. I (the commentator) say: One might object that if the basis of this ruling is this reasoning, then there would be no benefit in saying 'then it became vinegar'; rather it would suffice to say 'if one pawns grape juice for ten and it becomes wine, it remains a pawn for ten' because the same reasoning applies. The author of al-‘Inaya said: One might say that insofar as the substance is concerned, initial and continuing are the same, so what is the difference? He responded: This is true when the substance remains, but here the substance changes in legal terms with the change of description, so it differs from that principle. I (the commentator) say: His statement 'then it became vinegar and it is worth ten' indicates that the consideration in increase and decrease is value, but it is not so; rather the consideration is quantity because grape juice and vinegar are measured items. A decrease in value without a decrease in quantity does not cause any reduction of the debt, as mentioned in the case of a broken heart. It only gives the option to the pawner. So the ruling: if some of the quantity is reduced, a corresponding part of the debt is reduced; otherwise not. And the phrase 'then it became vinegar' indicates that the pawner is a Muslim and the creditor is a Muslim. If it were a dhimmi, it is stated in al-Mabsut: If a dhimmi pawns wine with another dhimmi, and it becomes vinegar, it does not reduce the debt because the change from bitterness to sourness decreases its value in their estimation, but the substance remains. So it remains a pawn, just as if a heart-shaped pawn breaks but the weight remains. Then according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the pawner has the option: if he wishes, he may redeem with the full debt and take it, or he may claim wine like his wine and it becomes...
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This separate chapter (fasl) addresses the unusual case of pawning grape juice that undergoes transformation into wine (khamr) and then into vinegar (khal). The key ruling: if the final vinegar has the same value as the original juice, the pawn remains valid for the original debt. The reasoning is based on the salability of the substance: wine, though not initially salable for Muslims, is salable as an existing commodity (for non-Muslims) and thus can be a valid pawn. The commentator refines the view, pointing out that for measured items like juice and vinegar, quantity (not value) is the criterion for reduction of debt. He also distinguishes the case of Muslim vs. dhimmi pawners: if both are dhimmis, the pawn remains valid even if the value decreases, because the substance remains. The passage includes a critical discussion of the reasoning from al-‘Inaya and al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
عصير (asir): Grape juice, a measured item (makil/mawzun).
خمر (khamr): Wine, which for Muslims is not salable at initiation but is salable as an existing commodity for dhimmis.
خلاق (khalal): Vinegar, a permissible substance.
كدتي (muqaddarat): Measured items (by weight or volume).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Division of Debt When Pledged Property Increases
Explains division of debt with pledged slave woman and offspring.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for dividing debt when a pledged slave woman gives birth and explain the reasoning behind the division.

Core Idea
The offspring becomes a pledge only at redemption; its value at that time determines its share of the debt.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a nuanced aspect of pledge (rahn) law: how to handle the debt when a pledged slave woman gives birth or additional property is added. The ruling hinges on treating the offspring as a branch of the mother and determining its share at redemption, not at birth. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly apportioning debt among multiple pledged items.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the case: a pledged slave woman gives birth, and/or additional property is pledged. The debt must be divided between the original item and the new item(s).
The text also covers a case where the mother becomes defective (one-eyed).
2
State the General Rule
The debt is divided into two halves. One half is based on the mother's value at the time of taking possession (qabd); the other half is based on the child's value at the time of redemption (fikak). If the mother's value decreases (e.g., due to defect), her share of the debt is reduced proportionally.
The child's value is assessed at redemption because that is when it becomes an independent pledge.
3
Explain the Rationale
The child is a branch (far') of the mother (asl). Therefore, the ruling on the mother extends to the child as a follower. The mother's value at contract is used because the increase (child) is considered attached to her.
This is a form of qiyas (analogy) based on the principle of taba'iyyah (followership).
4
Apply to the Currency Example
In al-Muntaqa, a man pledges one dinar for ten dirhams, then adds another dinar, and the creditor adds five dirhams. The general rule treats both dinars as covering the total fifteen. Abu Hanifa disagrees, arguing that increasing the debt of a pledge is invalid.
Abu Hanifa's view: first dinar and two-thirds of second for original ten; one-third of second for half of the extra five as pledge; the other half as unsecured debt.
5
Note the Underlying Principle
The offspring only becomes an intended (maqsud) part of the pledge at redemption because possession returns to it. Increasing the debt of a pledge is not permissible; an increase in debt is a new obligation.
This principle governs all cases of increase in pledged property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The pledged slave woman after she became one-eyed gave birth to a child worth a thousand, so the debt is divided into two halves on her value on the day of taking possession and on the value of the child on the day of redemption. Then what fell to the mother, half of it is nullified by the one-eyedness, so the mother and child remain with three-fourths of the debt. Its issues are in chapters: One of them is about the pledged slave woman when she gives birth and then an addition is made to the pledge. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining how debt is divided when a pledged slave woman gives birth and additional property is added. The author first states the general rule: the debt is divided based on the value of the mother at the time of contract and the value of the child at redemption. Then he explains the reasoning: because the child is a branch of the mother, its ruling follows hers. He then gives an example from al-Muntaqa involving a dinar and dirhams, and presents Abu Hanifa's view on the matter, emphasizing that increasing the debt of a pledge is not permissible. Finally, he outlines three chapters under which the issues fall: the first when a pledged slave woman gives birth and additional property is added, the second when one of two pledged slave women gives birth and additional property is added, and the third when a pledged slave woman becomes one-eyed and additional property is added.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge or collateral given to secure a debt.
قيمة يوم القبض (qimat yawm al-qabd): The value of the pledged item on the day of taking possession by the creditor.
قيمة يوم الفكاك (qimat yawm al-fikak): The value of the pledged item at the time of redemption.
مقصود (maqsud): Intended; refers to the status of the offspring when it becomes a direct part of the pledge.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Followership; the concept that the offspring follows the ruling of the mother.

Division of Debt When the Pledged Mother Dies and the Child Becomes an Original Pledge
Ruling with proof: calculation of debt division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the division of debt when a pledged mother dies and the child becomes an original pledge, accounting for changes in the child's value.

Core Idea
When a pledged mother dies, her child becomes an original pledge and the debt is divided proportionally based on values at contract and redemption.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details a nuanced scenario in pledge (rahn) transactions: a slave woman pledged for a debt gives birth, then dies, and an additional slave is added. The author explains how the remaining debt is divided between the child and the added slave, with subcases for the child's death, appreciation, and depreciation. Understanding these calculations is crucial for correctly applying the law of pledges in complex situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
Read the first part: a slave girl worth 1000 is pledged for 1000, she gives birth to a child worth 1000, then she dies, and an additional slave worth 1000 is added. Note the values and the debt.
2
Determine the division of debt at the time of the mother's death
The debt is divided equally between the mother and the child because they have equal value (500 each). The mother's share falls due to her death, and the child becomes an original pledge. The remaining debt (500) is split between the added slave and the child (250 each).
Key principle: the child becomes an original pledge only if it survives to redemption time.
3
Apply the rule when the child dies
If the child dies before redemption, it is as if it never existed; its share of debt disappears, and the entire debt is deemed to have fallen with the mother. The added slave was pledged for no standing debt, so the increase is void and the pledgor can recover the added slave without payment.
4
Apply the rule when the child's value changes (appreciation)
If the child's value increases to 2000 at redemption, reconsider the division. The mother's value at contract was 1000, total debt 1000. Now the child's value is 2000. The debt is divided into thirds: 1/3 (333.33) attributable to the mother (value 1000) and 2/3 (666.66) to the child (value 2000). Since the mother died, 1/3 of debt is extinguished; the remaining 2/3 must be paid to redeem both the child and the added slave.
Only the child's value at redemption matters; the mother's value is fixed at contract.
5
Apply the rule when the child's value decreases (depreciation)
If the child's value drops to 500 at redemption, the mother's value is still 1000 at contract. Total debt 1000. The mother's share is 2/3 (since her value is double the child's) and the child's share is 1/3. So 2/3 of debt (666.66) falls with the mother; remaining 1/3 (333.33) is owed to redeem the child and the added slave.
The child's value at redemption determines its share of debt proportionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو رهن جارية بألف تساوي ألفاً فولدت ما يساوي ألفا ثم ماتت الأمة فزاد الرهن ولداً يساوي ألفاً افتكهما المرتهن بنصف الدين لأن الدين انقسم عليهما نصفين لاستوائهما في القيمة، ثم حصة الأم خمسمائة قد سقطت بهلاكها وصار الولد أصلاً في الرهن بشرط بقائه إلى وقت الفكاك فدخلت الزيادة عليه وانقسمت الخمسمائة الباقية على العبد الزائد والولد نصفين، وإن مات الولد استرد العبد بلا شيء لأنه لما هلك الولد صار كأنه لم يملك أصلاً فتبين أنه لا قسط له من الدين لأنه لم يبق إلى وقت الفكاك فتبين أن كل الدين ساقط بهلاك الأم وأنه زاد العبد وليس هناك دين قائم فكانت الزيادة باطلة فكان له أن يسترده بغير شيء، ولو لم يمت ولكنه زاد حتى صار يساوي ألفين يفتك الأول والعبد بثلثي الدين لأن في انقسام الدين إنما تعتبر قيمة الولد وقت الفكاك وقيمة الأم وقت العقد ألف فانقسم الدين أثلاثاً فسقط ثلثه بهلاك الأم وبقي ثلثاه تبعاً للولد. ولو نقص فصار يساوي خمسمائة افتكه بثلث الدين لأنه تبين أنه سقط بهلاك الأم ثلثا الدين انقسم عليهما أثلاثاً ثلثه بإزاء الولد لأن قيمته يوم الفكاك ثلث قيمة الأم وقت العقد.
If someone pledges a slave girl worth a thousand for a thousand, and she gives birth to what is worth a thousand, then the mother dies, and the pledge is increased by a slave worth a thousand, the pledgee redeems both for half the debt because the debt was divided between them equally due to equality of value. Then the mother's share, five hundred, fell due to her destruction, and the child becomes an original pledge subject to its survival until the time of redemption, so the increase enters upon it and the remaining five hundred is divided between the added slave and the child in halves. And if the child dies, the slave is returned without anything because when the child died, it becomes as if it was never owned, so it becomes clear that it has no share of the debt because it did not survive to the time of redemption, so it becomes clear that the entire debt fell due to the destruction of the mother, and that he added the slave and there is no standing debt, so the increase is void, so he can take it back without anything. And if it did not die but increased until it became worth two thousand, he redeems the first and the slave with two-thirds of the debt because in the division of the debt, only the value of the child at the time of redemption is considered, and the mother's value at the time of contract is a thousand, so the debt is divided into thirds, so one-third fell due to the mother's death, and two-thirds remain following the child. And if it decreased until it became worth five hundred, he redeems it with one-third of the debt because it becomes clear that due to the mother's death, two-thirds of the debt fell, which was divided between them in thirds, one-third corresponding to the child because its value on the day of redemption is one-third of the mother's value at the time of contract.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that details the scenario where a pledged slave woman dies after giving birth, and a additional slave is added as pledge. The author explains the division of the remaining debt based on the values at the time of contract and redemption. He covers subcases: the child's death, increase in value, and decrease in value. The key principle is that the child becomes an original pledge (أصلاً في الرهن) once the mother dies, and the debt is divided accordingly.

Key Terms
أصل في الرهن (asl fi al-rahn): The primary pledged property that bears the debt directly.
فكاك (fikak): Redemption, the act of paying the debt to release the pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the child's value increases to 2000 at redemption (mother's value at contract is 1000), what fraction of the original debt is extinguished due to the mother's death?
A) 1/3
B) 1/2
C) 2/3
D) 3/4

Key Takeaway
When a pledged mother dies, her child becomes an original pledge, and the debt is divided proportionally based on values at contract (for the mother) and at redemption (for the child).

Debt Division with Mother Slave and Additional Slave
Explains debt division with mother slave appreciation and added slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a child follower (taba') in a pledge does not receive an independent share when the mother is alive, and distinguish this case from when the mother dies.

Core Idea
The follower's share is merged with the original until the original is lost.

In Hanafi law of pledges (rahn), when a slave mother is pledged and later appreciates, and an additional slave is added as pledge, the debt must be divided correctly. The key is the status of the child: as long as the mother is alive, the child is a follower (taba') and its value is included in the mother's share. This lesson unpacks the rationale and the contrasting scenario when the mother dies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) mother alive and appreciates, with an added slave; (2) mother dies, then the child is added. Understand each case's facts.
Focus on the legal consequence of the mother's survival.
2
Apply the principle of taba' (follower)
When the mother is present, the child is a follower. In division, the follower does not get an independent share; it is subsumed under the original. So the debt is divided between the mother (including child's value) and the added slave.
The child's value is not separately counted.
3
Contrast with mother's death
If the mother dies, the child becomes an original pledge because the original is lost. Then the debt division is between the child and the added slave.
The child shifts from follower to original.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason: the follower enters with the original in division (al-taba' yadkhul ma'a al-asl fi al-inqisam). As long as the original is present, the follower's share is not considered separately.
This is a core Hanafi principle in pledges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو نمت الأم وزاد العبد ففيه نصف الدين وفي الأم وولدها نصفه لأن الجارية لما كانت قائمة كان الولد تبعاً لها في الرهن فما لم يظهر نصيب الأصل لا يعتبر التبع في الانقسام لأن التبع يدخل مع الأصل في الانقسام فانقسم الدين على الجارية وعلى العبد الزائد نصفين بخلاف ما إذا ماتت الجارية ثم زيد الولد لأن الولد صار أصلاً في الرهن بفوات الأصل لأن اتباع القائم للهلاك لا أن يجعل أصلاً فاعتبرناه في فانقسم ما بقي من الدين على الولد والعبد الزيادة
And if the mother increases in value and a slave is added, then half the debt is in it, and in the mother and her child is half of it, because as long as the slave girl is present, the child is a follower of her in the pledge, so as long as the share of the original does not appear, the follower is not considered in the division, because the follower enters with the original in the division. So the debt is divided between the slave girl and the added slave in halves, contrary to when the slave girl dies and then the child is added, because the child becomes an original pledge due to the loss of the original, because following the existing one is due to destruction, not that it becomes an original. So we considered it, and then the remaining debt was divided between the child and the added slave.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that covers the scenario where the mother (the original pledged slave) appreciates in value and an additional slave is added as pledge. The author explains that the child remains a follower of the mother as long as the mother is alive, so the debt is divided between the mother and the added slave, with the child's value included in the mother's share. This contrasts with the case where the mother dies, as explained in the previous lesson.

Key Terms
تبع (taba'): A follower; the child is a follower of the mother in the pledge when the mother is present.
أصل (asl): The original; the mother slave is the original pledge, and the child is its follower.
رهن (rahn): Pledge; collateral given to secure a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when the mother (original pledged slave) is alive and appreciates, how is the child treated in the division of debt?
A) As an original pledge
B) As a follower of the mother
C) As independent but with a reduced share
D) Ignored entirely

Key Takeaway
A follower (taba') does not get an independent share in the division of a pledged debt as long as the original collateral is present.

Partial Payment and Adding a New Pledge
Ruling with proof on partial debt payment and new pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of partial debt payment on a newly added pledge and distinguish the rulings when the payment is made with good currency versus counterfeit currency.

Core Idea
A new pledge covers only the remaining debt; the currency type determines whether partial payment actually reduces the debt.

This passage examines a nuanced scenario in pledge law: a debtor pays part of a secured debt and then adds a new item as a pledge. The ruling hinges on whether the payment is considered a true satisfaction of part of the debt. The author explains how the new pledge's coverage is determined and discusses special cases involving the quality of the currency used for payment, drawing an analogy with the mukatib contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial pledge
A slave girl worth 1000 is pledged for a debt of 1000. Then 500 is paid, and a slave worth 1000 is added as an extra pledge. The question is: what part of the new pledge is valid?
The new pledge is the slave added after partial payment.
2
State the principle for increase in pledge
The increase (new pledge) only covers the remaining debt (qā'im), not the paid portion (sāqiṭ). The pledge is for satisfaction and fulfillment of an existing debt; debt that is fallen or extinguished cannot be secured.
Key Arabic: 'الزيادة في الرهن إنما تصح في حق القائم من الدين دون الساقط'
3
Calculate the division of the remaining debt
The remaining debt is 500. The new slave is worth 1000. The old slave girl's half (500) is still occupied as a guarantor for the paid portion, so the remaining 500 is divided proportionally: two-thirds on the new slave and one-third on the old slave girl.
The division reflects that the old pledge continues to secure the paid amount, so its remaining capacity is reduced.
4
Analyze the effect of payment currency: good dirham (sutūqa)
If the creditor receives a good dirham different from the debt's genus, it is not a satisfaction; it is a sale. Thus the entire debt remains, and the new pledge covers the full original debt.
ستوقة means a good, genuine coin of a different type.
5
Contrast with counterfeit currency (zuyūf)
Counterfeit coins are of the same genus, so they satisfy the debt partially. If the creditor returns them due to defect, the satisfaction stands but the creditor has recourse. The new pledge covers only the remaining debt.
زيوف are defective but of the same type; they do not change the genus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رهن جارية تساوي ألفاً بألف فقضاه من الدين خمسمائة ثم زاد عبداً يساوي ألفاً فالعبد رهن بثلثي الخمسمائة الباقية لأن الزيادة في الرهن إنما تصح في حق القائم من الدين دون الساقط لأن الرهن استيفاء وإيفاء الساقط والمتوفى لا يتصور والقائم من الدين خمسمائة فيقسم على قيمة العبد وعلى نصف قيمة الجارية لأن نصفها بقي مشغولاً بالخمسمائة المستوفاة مضموناً بها، فإن استيفاء الدين لا يخرج الرهن من أن يكون مضموناً حتى لو هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن يسترد الراهن المستوفي فانقسمت الخمسمائة الباقية أثلاثاً ثلثاه في العبد الزيادة، فإن وجد المرتهن ما اقتضاه ستوقة فالعبد والجارية رهن بألف لأن الستوقة ليست من جنس حقه فبقبضها لا مقتضياً يصير ومستوفياً فتبين أن جميع الدين كان قائماً حتى زاده العبد، وإن وجده زيوفاً أو مستحقاً فرده فالجارية رهن بألف والعبد رهن معها بخمسمائة وليس للراهن أخذ الجارية بخمسمائة حتى الألف، وإن أدى خمسمائة فله أن يأخذ العبد لأن الزيوف من جنس حقه إلا أن به عيباً يؤدي ووجود العيب لا يبدل جنسه كما في الصرف والسلم فصار مقتضياً ومستوفياً لا مستبدلاً، فحين زاد العبد كان القائم من الدين خمسمائة فصار العبد زيادة قيمة فانقسمت الخمسمائة عليها، والرد بعيب الزيادة ينقص القبض من الأصل ولكن لم يتبين أنه لم يكن قابضاً ألا ترى المكاتب لا يبطل برد المولى المال بعيب الزيافة فلهذا كان العبد زيادة في خاصة.
If one pledges a slave girl worth a thousand for a thousand, then he pays five hundred of the debt, then he adds a slave worth a thousand, then the slave is a pledge for two-thirds of the remaining five hundred, because the increase in the pledge is only valid with respect to the existing debt, not the fallen portion, because the pledge is for satisfaction and fulfillment; the fallen and deceased cannot be imagined. The existing debt is five hundred, so it is divided on the value of the slave and on half the value of the slave girl, because half of her remained occupied by the satisfied five hundred as a guarantor. For the satisfaction of the debt does not remove the pledge from being guaranteed; even if the pledge is destroyed in the hand of the pledgee, the pledger recovers what was satisfied. So the remaining five hundred was divided into thirds, two-thirds in the added slave. If the pledgee finds what he collected to be a good dirham (ستوقة), then the slave and the slave girl are a pledge for a thousand, because the good dirham is not of the same type as his right, so by taking it, he does not become a claimer and satisfied, so it becomes clear that all the debt was existing until he added the slave. And if he finds them counterfeit or disputed and returns them, then the slave girl is a pledge for a thousand and the slave is a pledge with her for five hundred, and the pledger cannot take the slave girl for five hundred until the thousand. And if he pays five hundred, he may take the slave because the counterfeit is of the same type as his right, except that it has a defect that requires return, and the existence of the defect does not change its type, as in currency exchange and salam. So he became a claimer and satisficer, not a substitute. So when he added the slave, the existing debt was five hundred, so the slave became an increase in value, so the five hundred was divided upon it. And the return due to the defect of the increase diminishes the possession from the origin, but it does not become clear that he was not a possessor. Do you not see that the mukatib does not invalidate by the master's return of the money due to the defect of counterfeit? Therefore, the slave was an increase in particular.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that explains the complex scenario where a debtor pays part of the debt and then adds a new pledge. The key principle is that the new pledge only covers the remaining debt, not the paid portion. The text also discusses the effect of the quality of the payment: if the payment was in good currency (ستوقة), the entire debt is considered still existing because good currency is not the same as the debt type? Actually, the text says if the creditor receives a good dirham (ستوقة), that does not satisfy because it's not from the same genus? But in Hanafi fiqh, an exchange of different currencies is considered a sale, not settlement. This is a nuanced area. The author then discusses counterfeit money and the ruling that it is considered of the same genus, so the debt is satisfied and the new pledge only covers the remaining.

Key Terms
ستوقة (sutūqa): A good, genuine dirham (or coin) that is not counterfeit.
زيوف (zuyūf): Counterfeit coins that are defective but still of the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a debtor pays part of the debt and then adds a new pledge, what does the new pledge cover?
A) The entire original debt
B) Only the remaining unpaid portion
C) The paid portion only
D) Half of the unpaid portion

Key Takeaway
A new pledge added after partial payment secures only the remaining debt, and payment with a different genus currency does not reduce the secured debt.

Dividing Debt Among Multiple Pledged Items After Partial Destruction
A ruling demonstrating the proportional division of debt when pledged items are destroyed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the loss distribution when multiple pledged items are partially destroyed, following the Hanafi method of proportional division.

Core Idea
When a pledged item is destroyed, its share of the debt falls proportionally; offspring become independent pledges upon the mother's death.

This lesson examines a complex scenario from the Hanafi fiqh of pledges (rahn). Two slave girls are pledged for a debt of 1000, each worth 1000. A slave is added as further collateral. One girl gives birth to a child worth 1000, then the mother dies, and later the added slave dies. The calculation recalculates how much of the debt is lost and how the remaining collateral covers it. Mastering this proportioning method is essential for dealing with fluctuating collateral values in Hanafi mu'amalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify all items and initial values
List all pledged items and their values: two slave girls (each 1000), added slave (value not explicitly given but inferred to be 1000 from the calculation), and the child (1000). The original debt is 1000.
The added slave's value is assumed to be 1000 for the calculation to work.
2
Determine the initial debt division among the mother and child
The debt of 1000 is divided between the mother (the first slave girl) and her child in halves: each covers 500. This is because the mother dies leaving a child, and the child becomes an original pledge.
The child becomes 'aslan' (original) after the mother's death.
3
Apply the effect of the mother's death
The mother's share of 500 is lost (since she is destroyed). The child retains its share of 500, and its value is 1000, so it continues to cover 500 of the debt.
The mother's value (1000) is also gone; her share of debt is written off.
4
Allocate the added slave between remaining items
The added slave (value 1000) enters with two-thirds of his value to the remaining second slave girl (value 1000) and one-third to the child (value 1000). This is because the child is now an original pledge and shares the burden.
The proportions are based on the remaining values after the mother's death.
5
Compute the final loss using proportional division
The remaining debt is 500 (from the child's share) plus 500 from the second girl? Wait, the second girl still has 1000, but the debt was 1000 total. Actually, after mother's death, the debt is still 1000, but the mother's share (500) is lost? The text says the loss is 525. This step requires dividing the 500 (from child's side) and the 1000 from the second girl's side among the items proportionally, resulting in a total loss of 525.
The exact arithmetic is corrupted in the source; the method is what matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رهن جاريتين بألف تساوي كل واحدة ألفاً وزاده عبد فولدت إحداهما ولداً يساوي ألفاً ثم ماتت الأم ثم مات العبد يموت خمسمائة وخمسة وعشرون لأن نصف الألف يسقط بهلاك إحدى الجاريتين لأن قيمتها ألف وذلك لأن الألف انقسم عليها وعلى ولدها نصفين فسقط بهلاكها حصتها وهي خمسمائة وبقي الولد بخمسمائة، وفي الجارية الباقية ألف والعبد الزائد يدخل ثلثاه الجارية الباقية وثلثه مع الولد لأن الولد صار أصلاً لفوات متبوعه مع فدخل في الخمسمائة التي في الولد فيقسم ذلك على قيمة الولد وهي ألف وعلى ثلث قيمة العبد وذلك ثلاثمائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث فاجعل هذا القدر بينهما فتكون قيمة الولد ثلاثة أسهم، وانقسمت الخمسمائة أرباعاً ربعها في ثلث العبد الزائد وثلاثة أرباعها في الولد. وأما الألف التي في الجارية الباقي انقسمت على قيمتها وهي ألف وعلى قيمة ثلثي العبد الزيادة وذلك ستمائة وستة وستون وثلثان فاجعل التفاوت بين الأقل والأكثر بينهما وذلك ثلاثمائة أن عتق الخمسمائة
If one pledges two slave girls for a thousand, each worth a thousand, and adds a slave, then one of them gives birth to a child worth a thousand, then the mother dies, then the slave dies, the loss is five hundred and twenty-five? In the remaining slave girl is a thousand, and the added slave enters: two-thirds of him with the remaining slave girl and one-third with the child, because the child became an original due to the loss of its follower, so it entered into the five hundred that is in the child, so that is divided on the value of the child which is a thousand, and on one-third of the value of the slave, which is three hundred and thirty-three and a third. So make this amount between them, so the value of the child becomes three shares, and the five hundred is divided into quarters: a quarter in one-third of the added slave, and three quarters in the child. The text appears to be incomplete or corrupted, but the method involves valuing each item and dividing the debt proportionally. The key point is that when the mother of the child dies, the child becomes an original pledge and its share is reallocated.

Voluntary Payment of Another's Dowry: Recovery Rights on Early Divorce
Ruling on voluntary payment of another's dowry and recovery upon early divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a volunteer pays another's dowry and the wife divorces before consummation, and explain the distinction between payment by order and voluntary payment.

Core Idea
A volunteer who pays another's dowry recovers half if divorce occurs before consummation; voluntary payment retains ownership.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a situation where a third party voluntarily pays the dowry for another's wife. If the wife divorces before consummation, the mahr is halved, and the question arises: can the volunteer recover? The ruling clarifies that he can recover half, because the voluntary payment did not transfer ownership. The author draws an analogy with buying a slave to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
A volunteer pays another's dowry; if divorce before consummation, he recovers half of what he paid.
2
Note the analogy
Similar to buying a slave where a volunteer pays the price and the slave is returned due to a defect; in that case, the volunteer recovers the full price.
The analogy highlights the principle of proportional recovery.
3
Understand the distinction
Payment by order transfers ownership via guarantee; voluntary payment does not, so the volunteer retains ownership of the money.
This distinction determines whether recovery is full or half.
4
Apply to the case
Since the dowry obligation halves upon divorce, the volunteer recovers the unneeded half.
The volunteer's ownership right allows him to reclaim the excess.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل دفع مهر امرأة غيره تطوعاً فطلقت المرأة قبل الوطء رجع المتطوع بنصف ما أدى، وكذا لو اشترى عبداً وتطوع رجل بأداء ثمنه ثم رد العبد بعيب رجع المتطوع بما أدى عنهما فصار كأدائهما بإذنهما قلنا : أنه إذا قضى بأمرها رجع عليها بما أدى فملكاه بالضمان وهنا لم يملكاه فيبقى على ملك المتطوع والله تعالى أعلم
A man paid the dowry of another's wife voluntarily. If the woman is divorced before consummation, the volunteer recovers half of what he paid. Similarly, if he buys a slave and a man voluntarily pays its price, and then the slave is returned due to a defect, the volunteer recovers what he paid. So it becomes as if they paid with their permission. We say: if he pays on her order, he recovers from her what he paid, so they become owners by guarantee. Here they did not own it, so it remains the property of the volunteer. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage addresses a situation where someone voluntarily pays another's dowry. If the wife divorces before consummation, the volunteer is entitled to recover half of what he paid. The author draws an analogy with buying a slave where a third party voluntarily pays the price. If the slave is returned due to a defect, the volunteer can recover his payment. The key distinction is between payment by order (where the payer becomes owner by guarantee) and voluntary payment (where the payer retains ownership). The passage concludes that the volunteer retains ownership of the amount paid, not the original recipient.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act; doing something without being obliged.
مهر (mahr): Dowry; mandatory payment by the husband to the wife upon marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man voluntarily pays the dowry of another's wife and then the wife divorces before consummation, how much can the volunteer recover?
A) All of what he paid.
B) Half of what he paid.
C) Nothing.
D) Double what he paid.

Key Takeaway
A volunteer who pays another's dowry recovers half if divorce occurs before consummation, as the payment remains his property.
